5 min
Why Real Definition Is Extremely Difficult
Declares real definition extremely difficult, leading to its abandonment by Illuminationists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two confusions that make real definition difficult and explain why the Illuminationists abandoned it.

Core Idea
Real definition fails because genus and common accident are easily confused.

This lesson explores a key epistemological challenge in definition theory: the extreme difficulty of constructing a real definition (al-tahdid al-haqiqi). The author declares that the genus (jins) can be mistaken for a common accident ('arad 'amm), and the differentia (fasl) for a specific property (khassa). Because of this subtlety, the Illuminationist school (al-Ishrāqiyya) entirely dropped real definition from consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two pairs
The passage states that genus resembles common accident, and differentia resembles specific property. Find these pairs in the Arabic: الجنس مشتبه بالعرض العام، والفصل بالخاصة.
2
Understand the confusion
Real definition requires precise knowledge of genus and differentia. Mistaking a common accident for the genus produces a false definition. Why is this confusion so problematic?
The distinction is subtle; even experts may disagree.
3
Note the consequence
The Illuminationists (al-Ishrāqiyya) abandoned real definition because of this difficulty. Does this mean they rejected all definitions or only real definitions?
They still used descriptions (rusūm) and nominal definitions.
4
Reflect on the epistemological lesson
If even skilled logicians can confuse genus with common accident, what does that imply about the reliability of definitions? How does this affect the project of defining terms in Islamic sciences?
This shows why many scholars prefer to rely on descriptions rather than real definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالتَّحْدِيدُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ عَسِيرٌ جِدًّا، فَإِنَّ الْجِنْسَ مُشْتَبِهٌ بِالْعَرَضِ الْعَامِّ، وَالْفَصْلَ بِالْخَاصَّةِ، وَالْفَرْقُ بَيْنَهُمَا مِنَ الْغَوَامِضِ، وَفِي الْحَدِّ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ عِلْمِهَا، وَلَذَا أَسْقَطَهُ الْإِشْرَاقِيَّةُ عَنِ الِاعْتِبَارِ.
And real definition is very difficult, for the genus is confused with the common accident, and the differentia with the specific property, and the distinction between them is among the subtle matters. And in definition, knowledge of them is necessary, and therefore the Illuminationists (Ishraqiyyun) dropped it from consideration.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage declares the extreme difficulty of arriving at a real definition (al-tahdid al-haqiqi). The difficulty arises because the genus (jins) can be mistaken for a common accident ('arad 'amm), and the differentia (fasl) can be confused with a specific property (khassa). Distinguishing them requires deep insight. Since a valid definition presupposes this knowledge, the Illuminationist school (al-Ishraqiyyun) abandoned the project of real definition altogether.

Key Terms
الْعَرَض الْعَامّ
الْخَاصَّة
الْإِشْرَاقِيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Illuminationists (al-Ishraqiyyun) abandon real definition according to the passage?
A) Because definitions are unnecessary for knowledge.
B) Because the genus and common accident are easily confused, and the distinction is too subtle.
C) Because they believed only simple things can be defined.
D) Because they preferred to use only descriptions.

Key Takeaway
The difficulty of distinguishing genus from common accident and differentia from specific property led the Illuminationists to abandon real definition as unattainable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Consider the standard definition of a human as 'rational animal.' Identify the genus and differentia. Then, argue whether 'rational' could be mistaken for a specific property (khāṣṣa) rather than a true differentia. Use the passage's logic.
?
Task 2: Find an example from the history of Islamic logic (e.g., in works of al-Ghazali or Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) where a definition was rejected because the author argued that what was thought to be a genus was actually a common accident. Summarize the example in one paragraph.

Hadd and Rasm
beginner
5 min
Types of Rasm (Description) and Their Purpose
Describes the types of rasm and their purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of rasm (description) and explain its purpose of distinction as opposed to essential definition.

Core Idea
Rasm distinguishes without revealing essence; it uses accidents or mixtures.

We have completed the study of essential definitions (hadd). Now we turn to descriptions (rasm), which serve a different purpose. While a hadd reveals the essence of a thing, a rasm merely distinguishes it from other things using its accidental attributes, sometimes mixed with essential ones. Understanding rasm is crucial when we cannot access the essence but still need a precise distinguisher.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish hadd from rasm
Recall that hadd uses genus and differentia to reveal the essence. Rasm, by contrast, does not aim at essence; it only aims at distinguishing the thing. The passage explicitly says: 'laysa al-gharaḍ minhu illa al-tamayyuz' (its purpose is only distinction).
Hadd = essential definition; Rasm = description by accidents.
2
Identify the two types of rasm
The passage states that rasm may be either purely by accidents ('awarid) or mixed with essential attributes (dhatiyyat). The purely accidental type can have a scope that is more general, equal, or more specific than the thing described, provided that the thing is not essential to the accident.
Mixed rasm combines accidents and essentials, but still only aims at distinction.
3
Understand the condition for accidental rasm
For a purely accidental rasm, the accident used must not be such that the described thing is essential to it. This condition prevents circularity; the accident should not depend on the thing's essence.
Example: describing 'human' as 'laughing' (accident) is fine; 'laughing' is not essential to humans.
4
Grasp the sole purpose: distinction
The passage emphasizes that the only goal of any rasm is tamayyuz (distinction). Unlike hadd which reveals inner essence (kunh), rasm merely marks the thing off from others. This is the key functional difference.
Tamayyuz is a valid logical goal when essence is unknown or unnecessary for the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هَذَا كُلُّهُ فِي الْحَدِّ، بَقِيَ الْكَلَامُ فِي الرَّسْمِ، فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ قَدْ يَكُونُ بِالْعَوَارِضِ، سَوَاءً كَانَ أَعَمَّ أَوْ مُسَاوِيًا لِلْمَرْسُومِ، أَوْ أَخَصَّ مِنْهُ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْمَرْسُومُ ذَاتِيًّا لَهُ، وَقَدْ يَكُونُ مُخْتَلِطًا مَعَ الذَّاتِيَّاتِ، وَلَيْسَ الْغَرَضُ مِنْهُ إِلَّا التَّمَيُّزُ.
All this concerning the definition. The discussion remains on the description. Know that it may be by accidents, whether more general, equal, or more specific than the described thing, if the described thing is not essential to it. And it may be mixed with essentials. Its purpose is only distinction.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on definition and moves to description (rasm). Rasm is a definiens that does not reveal the essence but merely distinguishes the thing. It can be composed purely of accidental attributes ('awarid), which may be broader, equal, or narrower in extension than the thing described, provided the described thing is not essential to the accident (i.e., the accident does not inhere in the essence). Alternatively, rasm can be a mixture of essentials and accidents. The only goal of rasm is distinction (tamayyuz), not essential definition.

Key Terms
الرَّسْم
الْعَوَارِض
التَّمَيُّز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the sole purpose of a description (rasm)?
A) To reveal the essence of the thing.
B) To distinguish the thing from others.
C) To list all essential attributes.
D) To provide a complete definition.

Key Takeaway
Rasm is a legitimate type of definiens that distinguishes a thing by its accidents (or mixture), without aiming to reveal its essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the following definition is a hadd or a rasm: 'Wine is a fermented grape beverage that intoxicates.' Justify your answer by referencing the attributes used.
?
Construct a rasm for 'ghusl' (ritual purification) using only accidental attributes (e.g., 'washing the whole body with water with intent'). Is this a mixed or pure accidental rasm?

The Conditions of a True Definition (Hadd)
Defines hadd with examples and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components required for a complete hadd (genus, differentia, and causes) and evaluate whether a given definition meets these conditions.

Core Idea
A real definition must include all causes of the thing — omitting any cause invalidates it.

In this passage, the author explains what constitutes a proper definition (hadd). Using the example of blindness and relational terms, he shows that a definition must include the subject, the essential attributes, and all causes. This lesson will walk you through the components of a hadd and how to check its completeness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definiendum in the Arabic. For example, in 'العمى عدم البصر عما من شأنه أن يكون بصيرا', the definiendum is 'al-ʿamā' (blindness).
2
Extract the genus and differentia
For blindness, the genus is 'عدم' (absence/lack) and the differentia is 'البصر عما من شأنه أن يكون بصيرا' (sight in that which ought to have sight).
3
Identify the causes included
The author insists on including all causes. In the blindness example, the subject (that which ought to have sight) and the privation (absence of sight) are causes. For relational definitions like fatherhood, the cause of correlation (the act of generation) must be included.
4
Test the definition's completeness
Check if the definition includes genus, differentia, and all necessary causes. Using the fatherhood example: genus (rational animal), differentia (masculinity, generating another rational animal), and cause of correlation (generation). If any cause is missing, the definition is incomplete.
5
Understand why true species cannot define
The passage says a true species (like 'man') cannot serve as a definiens because it is not a genus. It lacks the necessary universality to define other things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرف
يقال: العمى عدم البصر عما من شأنه أن يكون بصيرا، وفي تحديد المضاف الحقيقي من أخذ ذاتياته وموضوعه وأخذ المضاف الآخر وموضوعه وعلة التضايف، كما يقال في تحديد الأبوة: إضافة في رجل مقايسة إلى إضافة في رجل آخر حدثها مقايسة الأولى إضافته أولى حدثها بتولد الثاني من الأول، وفي تحديد المضاف المشهور من أخذ حد المضاف الآخر وعلة التضايف، كما يقال في تحديد الأب حيوان ناطق مع الذكورة، يتولد منه حيوان ناطق آخر، ولا بد في التحديد بحسب الحقيقة من أخذ علله، والاختلال بأحدها لا يجوز، كذا في الشفاء.
وَالْبَسِيطُ لَا يُحَدُّ؛ إذ ليس له جزء، وَقَدْ يُحَدُّ بِهِ إذا كان جزء لشيء آخر، وَالْمُرَكَّبُ يُحَدُّ جوازا، وَيُحَدُّ بِهِ، وَقَدْ لَا يُحَدُّ به، كالنوع الحقيقي. وَالتَّحْدِيدُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ عَسِيرٌ جِدًّا، فَإِنَّ الجنس مُشْتَبِهٌ بِالْعَرَضِ الْعَامِّ، وَالْفَصْلَ بِالْخَاصَّةِ، وَالْفَرْقُ بينهما مِنَ الْغَوَامِضِ، وفي الحد لا بد من علمها، ولذا أسقطه الإشراقية عن الاعتبار.
هذا كله في الحد، بقي الكلام في الرسم، فاعلم أنه قد يكون بالعوارض، سواء كان أعم أو مساويا للمرسوم، أو أخص منه إن لم يكن المرسوم ذاتيا له، وقد يكون مختلطا مع الذاتيات، وليس الغرض منه إلا التميز عن الأغيار كلاً أو بعضا، وما هو من الخاصة والجنس أتم مما سواه، وبه يعرف المقولة وغيرها من الأجناس.
Chapter on the definiens. It is said: Blindness is absence of sight from that which by nature ought to have sight. In defining the true relational (al-mudaf al-haqiqi), one takes its essentials and its subject, and takes the other relational and its subject and the cause of correlation, as is said in defining fatherhood: a relation in a man compared to a relation in another man, its occurrence based on the first's relation first occurring by the generation of the second from the first. In defining the common relational (al-mudaf al-mashhoor), one takes the definition of the other relational and the cause of correlation, as is said in defining father: a rational animal with masculinity, from whom another rational animal is generated. In definition according to reality, it is necessary to take its causes, and deficiency in any of them is impermissible. So in al-Shifa'. The simple is not defined, for it has no part, and it may be used to define (something else) if it is a part of something else. The composite is defined permissibly, and is used to define, and may not be used to define, like the true species. Real definition is extremely difficult; for the genus is confused with the common accident, and the differentia with the peculiar property, and the distinction between them is among the obscure matters. In definition, knowledge of them is necessary, so the Illuminists disregarded it. This is all concerning definition. Remains the discussion of description (rasm). Know that it may be by accidents, whether more general or equal to the described, or more specific if the described is not essential to it, and it may be mixed with essentials. Its purpose is only distinction from others entirely or partially, and what is from the peculiar property and genus is more complete than what else, and by it the category and other genera are known.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a definitional section on the rules of definition (hadd) and description (rasm). It begins by giving an example of defining the privation 'blindness' as absence of sight in something that ought to have sight, showing that a proper definition includes the subject and the privation. Then it discusses two types of relational definitions: the true relational (like fatherhood) requires taking the essentials, subject, the other relational, and the cause of correlation; the common relational (like father) requires only the definition of the other relational and the cause. The text emphasizes that a real definition must include all causes; omitting any cause invalidates it. Next, it states that the simple (basiṭ) which has no parts cannot be defined, but it can be used as a definiens for something else if it is a part. The composite (murakkab) can be defined and can serve as a definiens, though true species may not be used as definiens (since it is not a genus). Real definition (taḥdīd ḥaqīqī) is very difficult because genus is easily confused with common accident and differentia with peculiar property; the distinction is subtle. The Illuminists (Ishrāqiyyūn) abandoned definition for this reason. Then the passage turns to description (rasm), which uses accidents. It may be by co-extensive or broader accidents, or narrower if the described is not essential. It may mix with essentials. Its purpose is mere distinction, and the best rasm uses peculiar property and genus, as this helps in knowing categories and genera.

Key Terms
الحد
الجنس
الفصل
البسيط
المركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required in a real definition (hadd)?
A) Only genus and differentia
B) Genus, differentia, and all causes
C) Only causes
D) Only accidents

Key Takeaway
A real definition (hadd) must include the genus, differentia, and all causes of the thing; omitting any cause invalidates it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the example of 'father' (أب) from the passage, list the components of its definition according to the author: genus (rational animal), differentia (masculinity, generating another rational animal), and the cause of correlation (the act of generation). Then check whether this definition meets the requirement of including all causes.
?
Now consider the definition of 'wudu' in fiqh: 'washing the face and hands and wiping the head and washing the feet'. Identify what is missing from a complete hadd (e.g., intention, sequence) and explain why it would be an incomplete definition according to this lesson.

Description (Rasm) and the Difficulty of Real Definition
Explains rasm and highlights difficulty of hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish rasm from hadd, and explain why the Illuminists abandoned formal definition.

Core Idea
Rasm distinguishes by accidents; it is easier but less certain than hadd, which the Illuminists abandoned due to the subtlety of genus and differentia.

After discussing hadd, the author turns to rasm (description), which uses accidents to identify a thing. He also notes the extreme difficulty of real definition because genus is easily confused with common accident and differentia with peculiar property. This lesson clarifies the role of rasm and its limitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of rasm
The passage states that the purpose of rasm is 'التميز عن الأغيار' (distinction from others), not expressing essence.
2
Recognize the types of rasm
Rasm can use accidents that are more general (أعم), co-extensive (مساو), or more specific (أخص) if the described is not essential. It may also mix with essentials.
3
Compare hadd and rasm
Hadd requires genus, differentia, and all causes; rasm can use accidents and its goal is mere distinction, not essential definition.
4
Understand the difficulty of hadd
The passage explains that real definition is extremely difficult because genus resembles common accident and differentia resembles peculiar property, and the distinction is subtle. Therefore, the Illuminists disregarded definition.
5
Apply the distinction
Given a definition, decide if it is hadd or rasm based on whether it provides essential components and causes or just accidental distinguishing marks.

Source Text

Why did the Illuminists (الإشراقية) disregard definition according to the passage?

Key Takeaway
Rasm uses accidents to distinguish, while hadd requires essential causes; the subtlety of genus and differentia led the Illuminists to abandon formal definition.

Hadd and Rasm

5 min
The Genus and Differentia: Internal Composition in Definition
Explains how the mind abstracts genus and adds differentia internally to form definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the relationship between genus and differentia in a real definition (hadd) versus a complete description (rasm tamm).

Core Idea
The differentia is an internal determination, not an external addition.

In Islamic logic, definitions must capture the essence. This passage clarifies how the mind treats the genus as an independent concept and adds the differentia internally to produce a real definition. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify key terms
Locate the terms 'الجنس' (genus), 'الفصل' (differentia), and 'الرسم التام' (complete description) in the Arabic. Notice how they are defined.
These terms are foundational for definition theory.
2
Understand the mental abstraction
Recognize that the mind abstracts the genus as having an independent existence in consideration, even though it is vague. This allows addition.
This is a mental operation, not a claim about external reality.
3
Contrast internal vs external addition
Note that in hadd, the differentia is added internally (متضمن)، while in rasm tamm, the addition is external and attached for distinction. The text explicitly contrasts the two.
Internal addition means the differentia is implicit within the genus.
4
Apply the analogy of scattered pearls
The text compares the definition's constituents to scattered pearls—each meaning is distinct but not predicated of the other in that mode. Understand this as indicating actual multiplicity without unity of predication.
This illustrates that the definition is a composed whole.
5
Check the result of addition
Verify that when the genus becomes attained by adding the differentia, it does not become something else but remains the same genus, now realized. This means the definition is a realization, not a change.
The genus is not transformed into a new kind; it is specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ هَهُنَا مَبَاحِثُ الْأَوَّلُ: الْجِنْسُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مُبْهَما، لَكِنَّ الذِّهْنَ قَدْ يَخْلُقُ لَهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّعَقُلُ، أي لأجل تعقله، وُجُودًا مُنْفَرِدًا في اللحاظ، وَأَضَافَ إِلَيْهِ الجنس زِيَادَةٌ، وهي الفصل، لَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ مَعْنَى خَارِجٌ لَاحِقٌ بِهِ، كما في الرسم التام؛ فإنه أضيف الزيادة فيه على أنه لاحق لأجل تميزه عن الأغيار، بَلْ قَيَّدَهُ لِأَجَل تَحَصُّلِهِ وَتَعَيْنِهِ في نفسه؛ ليرتفع تزلزله، حال كون تلك الزيادة مُتَضَمِّنًا داخلا فِيهِ، فَإِذَا صَارَ الجنس مُحَصَّلًا بانضياف الزيادة لَمْ يَكُنْ شَيْئًا آخَرَ، بل يبقى جنسا؛ فَإِنَّ التَّحَصُّلَ لَيْسَ يُغَيِّرُهُ، بَلْ يُحَقِّقْهُ. فَإِذَا نَظَرْتَ إِلَى الْحَدِّ وَجَدْتَهُ مُؤَلَّفًا مِنْ عِدَّةِ مَعَانٍ، كُلٌّ مِنْهَا مُغَايِرُ لِلْآخَرِ، كَالدُّرَرِ الْمَنْثُورَةِ غَيْرُ الْآخَرِ بِنَحْوِ مِنَ الِاعْتِبَارِ، فَهُنَاكَ كَثرَةٌ بِالْفِعْلُ، فَلَا يُحْمَلُ أَحَدُهُمَا عَلَى الْآخَرَ؛ لعدم الاتحاد في هذا النحو من الوجود، وإن كان محمولا في نحو آخر منه، وَلَا عَلَى الْمَجْمُوعِ؛ فَإِن وجود الكل يغاير وجود الجزء.
Then here are investigations. The first: the genus. Even though it is vague, the mind creates for it, by virtue of conceptualization, an independent existence in consideration, and adds to it—the genus—an addition, which is the differentia, not as an external meaning attached to it, as in the complete description; for there the addition is made as attached for the sake of distinguishing it from others, but rather restricts it for the sake of its attainment and specification in itself, so that its oscillation is removed, while that addition is implicit and internal to it. So when the genus becomes attained by the addition of the addition, it does not become something else, but remains a genus; for attainment does not change it, but rather realizes it. So when you look at the definition, you find it composed of several meanings, each of which is different from the other, like scattered pearls, not the other in some consideration, so there is actual multiplicity. Thus one of them is not predicated of the other, due to lack of unity in this mode of existence, although it may be predicated in another mode; nor is it predicated of the whole, for the existence of the whole differs from the existence of the part.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is about the mental conception of genus in definition. It explains that although the genus (e.g., animal) is an indeterminate concept, the mind can treat it as having an independent existence. Then when the differentia (e.g., rational) is added, it is not as an external accident (like in a description where the addition is for distinction), but rather as an internal determination—the differentia is implicitly contained within the genus. By adding the differentia, the genus becomes specified and determined, but it does not become a completely new thing; it remains the same genus, now realized. The analogy of scattered pearls illustrates that in a definition, the constituent meanings are distinct but not predicated of each other in that context; also the whole is not predicated of the part. This is a nuanced discussion of how definition involves a mental composition of multiplicity while preserving the unity of the defined thing.

التحديد

A) It is an external accident attached to the genus for distinction.
B) It is an internal determination that realizes the genus.
C) It changes the genus into a different kind.
D) It is a mere description without essential connection.

Key Takeaway
In a real definition, the differentia is an internal determination that realizes the genus, not an external addition.

The Inherent Addition of Differentia in Definition
Explains the inherent addition of differentia to genus in hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the differentia is added to the genus in a proper definition (hadd) and how this differs from a complete description (rasm tamm).

Core Idea
The differentia does not change the genus; it realizes it.

In classical Islamic logic, a definition (hadd) is built from a genus (jins) and a differentia (fasl). But how exactly do these combine? Is the differentia just an external label added for distinction, or does it penetrate the genus itself? This passage clarifies that in a true definition, the differentia is added inherently, not as a supervenient attribute. Understanding this distinction is essential for constructing sound definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components of definition
Locate the discussion of genus (jins) and differentia (fasl). Note that the genus is described as ambiguous (mubham) in itself.
2
Compare two modes of addition
The passage contrasts two ways to add the differentia: as an external supervenient meaning (as in rasm tamm) vs. as an inherent qualification (as in hadd). What is the key difference?
3
Analyze the effect of inherent addition
When added inherently, the differentia determines the genus without changing its genus nature. The genus remains a genus; its determination realizes it, not alters it.
4
Test with an example
Consider the definition of 'man' as 'rational animal'. Show how 'animal' (genus) qualified by 'rational' (differentia) yields one concept without becoming something else.
The example appears in a later section but is used here for illustration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن الأغيار كلاً أو بعضا، وما هو من الخاصة والجنس أتم مما سواه، وبه يعرف المقولة وغيرها من الأجناس. ثم ههنا مباحث الأول: الجنس، وإن كان مبهمًا، لكن الذهن قد يخلق له من حيث التعقل، أي لأجل تعقله وجودًا منفردًا في اللحاظ، وأضاف إليه الجنس زيادة، وهي الفصل، لا على أنه معنى خارج لاحق به، كما في الرسم التام؛ فإنه أضيف الزيادة فيه على أنه لاحق لأجل تميزه عن الأغيار، بل قيده لأجل تحصله وتعيينه في نفسه؛ ليرتفع تزلزله، حال كون تلك الزيادة متضمنًا داخلا فيه، فإذا صار الجنس محصلاً بانضياف الزيادة لم يكن شيئًا آخر، بل يبقى جنسًا؛ فإن التحصيل ليس يغيره، بل يحققه. فإذا نظرت إلى الحد وجدته مؤلفًا من عدة معان، كل منها مغاير للآخر بنحو من الاعتبار، فهناك كثرة بالفعل، فلا يحمل أحدهما على الآخر؛ لعدم الاتحاد في هذا النحو من الوجود، وإن كان محمولا في نحو آخر منه، ولا على المجموع؛ فإن وجود الكل يغاير وجود الجزء. فصل في المعرف: وليس معنى الحد بهذا الاعتبار معنى المحدود المعقول، إذ الحد أمور والمحدود أمر واحد، لكن إذا لوحظ إلى إبهام أحدهما وقيد بالآخر متضمنًا فيه، ووصف توصيفًا لأجل التحصيل والتقويم كان شيئًا مؤديًا إلى الصورة الوحدانية التي للمحدود كاسبًا لها، فالحد علة للمحدود في هذا النحو من الوجود. ومن ههنا ظهر وجه آخر لعدم محمولية الحد في هذا النحو من الوجود. مثلًا الحيوان الناطق في تحديد الإنسان يفهم منه شيء واحد، هو بعينه الحيوان الذي ذلك الحيوان بعينه الناطق، كما أن العقد الحملي يفيد الصورة الاتحادية التي للموضوع مع المحمول في الخارج، إلا أن هناك، أي في عقد الحمل تركيبًا خبريًا، ففيه حكم، فيصح السكوت، وهنا، أي في الحد تركيب تقييدي، يفيد تصوير الاتحاد فقط، فمجموع التصورات المتعلقة بالأجزاء تفصيلًا هو الحد الموصل إلى التصور الواحد المتعلق بجميع الأجزاء إجمالاً، وهو المحدود. وذهب بعض أجلة المتأخرين إلى أن في التحديد لا يحصل صورة
From the others in whole or in part, and what belongs to the specific property and genus is more complete than what is other than it, and by it the category and other genera are known. Then here are discussions: the first: the genus, even if it is ambiguous, but the mind may create for it, from the perspective of intellection – i.e., for the sake of its intellection – an isolated existence in mental consideration, and he added to it (the genus) a surplus, which is the differentia, not on the basis that it is an external meaning supervening upon it, as in the complete description; for the surplus therein is added as supervening for the sake of distinguishing it from others. Rather, he qualified it for the sake of its being determined and specified in itself, so that its instability is removed, while that surplus is inherent and included in it. So when the genus becomes determined by the addition of the surplus, it does not become something else, but remains a genus; for determination does not change it, but realizes it. So when you consider the definition, you find it composed of several meanings, each of which is different from the other in some respect; there is actual multiplicity, so one of them is not predicated of the other, due to lack of union in this mode of existence, even if it is predicated in another mode, nor is it predicated of the whole, for the existence of the whole is different from the existence of the part. Chapter on the definition: And the meaning of the definition in this consideration is not the meaning of the definiendum as intellected; for the definition is multiple things and the definiendum is one thing. But when one considers the ambiguity of one of them and qualifies it by the other which is inherent in it, and describes it with a description for the sake of determination and rectification, it becomes something leading to and acquiring the unitary form which belongs to the definiendum. So the definition is a cause for the definiendum in this mode of existence. From this another aspect becomes apparent for the non-predicability of the definition in this mode of existence. For example, 'rational animal' in defining man is understood as one thing, which is the very animal that is the very same rational; just as the predicational compound gives the unitary form of the subject with the predicate in external existence, except that there – i.e., in the predicational compound – there is a predicative composition, so it contains a judgment, so silence is permissible. And here – i.e., in the definition – it is a restrictive composition which only gives a conceptualization of union. So the totality of the conceptualizations related to the parts in detail is the definition that leads to the single conceptualization related to all the parts collectively, and that is the definiendum. And some of the eminent later scholars held that in definition, no image is attained
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) explaining the nature of definition (hadd) in logic. It opens by discussing the genus (jins) and how the mind can consider it in isolation despite its ambiguity. The differentia (fasl) is then added not as an external attribute (as in complete description, al-rasm al-tamm) but as an inherent qualification that makes the genus determinate. The author emphasizes that this addition does not change the genus into something else; rather, it realizes it. The definition, though composed of multiple meanings (genus and differentia) that are distinct in some respects, does not allow one part to be predicated of the other in this mode of existence, because they are not unified in the same way as in a predicative judgment. The second part introduces a key distinction: the meaning of the definition (hadd) is not the same as the definiendum (mahdud) when considered separately; the definition is a cause (illa) that leads to the unitary conceptual form of the definiendum. The example of 'rational animal' (al-hayawan al-natiq) defining 'man' (al-insan) illustrates that the definition yields a single concept. The author then contrasts the definition with a predicational compound (al-'aqd al-hamli): the predicational compound involves a judgment (hukm) and allows for silence (sukut), while the definition is a restrictive composition (tarkib taqyidi) that only provides a conceptualization (taswir) of union. Finally, the passage notes that some later scholars disagree on whether a single image results from definition, but the main point stands: the definition, via its detailed parts, leads to a unified conceptualization of the definiendum.

Key Terms
الجنس
الفصل
الحد
الرسم التام
العقد الحملي
التركيب التقييدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) As an external supervenient meaning, like in complete description.
B) As an inherent qualification that determines the genus without changing it.
C) As a separate predicate that can be independently true.
D) As a synonym of the genus.

Key Takeaway
In a proper definition, the differentia is added inherently to the genus, determining it without altering its genus nature.

Defining vs. Predicating: The Difference Between Hadd and 'Aqd Hamli
Contrasts definition with predicational compound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a definition (hadd) from a predicational compound ('aqd hamli) and classify a given statement as one or the other.

Core Idea
Definition unifies without judgment; proposition judges without unifying.

A definition (hadd) and a predicational compound ('aqd hamli) may look similar, but they function differently. The passage contrasts them: a predicational compound involves a judgment (hukm) and allows silence (sukut), while a definition is a restrictive composition that only provides a conceptualization (taswir) of union. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly analyzing logical discourse in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of composition
Locate the discussion of 'restrictive composition' (tarkib taqyidi) and 'predicational compound' ('aqd hamli). Note which one involves a judgment.
2
Analyze the role of judgment
In the predicational compound, there is a judgment (hukm) that can be true or false. In the definition, there is no judgment; it only conceptualizes union.
3
Apply to an example
Consider 'al-insanu hayawan natiq' (Man is a rational animal). Is this a definition or a predication? The passage says it is a definition that yields one concept; but when said as a sentence, it can also be a predication. How do we decide?
The context determines whether it functions as a definition (restrictive) or a proposition (predicative).
4
Conclude with the unitary form
The definition gives the unitary form of the definiendum; the proposition gives a form that includes a truth claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن الأغيار كلاً أو بعضا، وما هو من الخاصة والجنس أتم مما سواه، وبه يعرف المقولة وغيرها من الأجناس. ثم ههنا مباحث الأول: الجنس، وإن كان مبهمًا، لكن الذهن قد يخلق له من حيث التعقل، أي لأجل تعقله وجودًا منفردًا في اللحاظ، وأضاف إليه الجنس زيادة، وهي الفصل، لا على أنه معنى خارج لاحق به، كما في الرسم التام؛ فإنه أضيف الزيادة فيه على أنه لاحق لأجل تميزه عن الأغيار، بل قيده لأجل تحصله وتعيينه في نفسه؛ ليرتفع تزلزله، حال كون تلك الزيادة متضمنًا داخلا فيه، فإذا صار الجنس محصلاً بانضياف الزيادة لم يكن شيئًا آخر، بل يبقى جنسًا؛ فإن التحصيل ليس يغيره، بل يحققه. فإذا نظرت إلى الحد وجدته مؤلفًا من عدة معان، كل منها مغاير للآخر بنحو من الاعتبار، فهناك كثرة بالفعل، فلا يحمل أحدهما على الآخر؛ لعدم الاتحاد في هذا النحو من الوجود، وإن كان محمولا في نحو آخر منه، ولا على المجموع؛ فإن وجود الكل يغاير وجود الجزء. فصل في المعرف: وليس معنى الحد بهذا الاعتبار معنى المحدود المعقول، إذ الحد أمور والمحدود أمر واحد، لكن إذا لوحظ إلى إبهام أحدهما وقيد بالآخر متضمنًا فيه، ووصف توصيفًا لأجل التحصيل والتقويم كان شيئًا مؤديًا إلى الصورة الوحدانية التي للمحدود كاسبًا لها، فالحد علة للمحدود في هذا النحو من الوجود. ومن ههنا ظهر وجه آخر لعدم محمولية الحد في هذا النحو من الوجود. مثلًا الحيوان الناطق في تحديد الإنسان يفهم منه شيء واحد، هو بعينه الحيوان الذي ذلك الحيوان بعينه الناطق، كما أن العقد الحملي يفيد الصورة الاتحادية التي للموضوع مع المحمول في الخارج، إلا أن هناك، أي في عقد الحمل تركيبًا خبريًا، ففيه حكم، فيصح السكوت، وهنا، أي في الحد تركيب تقييدي، يفيد تصوير الاتحاد فقط، فمجموع التصورات المتعلقة بالأجزاء تفصيلًا هو الحد الموصل إلى التصور الواحد المتعلق بجميع الأجزاء إجمالاً، وهو المحدود. وذهب بعض أجلة المتأخرين إلى أن في التحديد لا يحصل صورة
From the others in whole or in part, and what belongs to the specific property and genus is more complete than what is other than it, and by it the category and other genera are known. What is the key difference between a definition (hadd) and a predicational compound ('aqd hamli) according to the passage?

The Definition (Hadd) as a Composite Leading to the Unified Image of the Defined
Author explains that the definition (hadd) is not identical to the defined but leads to its unified image

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the definition (hadd) is not identical to the defined (mahdud) and how it leads to a single unified concept.

Core Idea
A definition is not just a list of parts; it is a composite that yields one unified image of the defined essence.

In this passage, the author distinguishes between the definition and the defined. While the definition is composed of genus and differentia, it is not a mere aggregation. Instead, it serves as a cause that produces the unitary mental image of the defined. This distinction is vital for understanding how definitions function in Islamic logic and why they are not predicated of the defined.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's main thesis
Find the sentence where the author states that the meaning of the definition is not the meaning of the defined. This is the central claim that the definition is a distinct entity that leads to the defined.
2
Trace the process from parts to unity
Observe how the author describes the composition: one part is ambiguous (mubham) and the other restricts it (yuqayyid). When combined, they produce a single image, not multiple.
3
Analyze the definition's causal role
Note that the author calls the definition a 'cause' (illa) for the defined in this mode of existence. This highlights that the definition is not merely a linguistic expression but an epistemic cause that brings about the conceptual image.
4
Differentiate definition from predicative proposition
Compare the restrictive composition (tarkib taqyidi) of definition with the predicative composition (tarkib khabari) of a proposition. The definition only gives a conceptual image (tasawwur), while a proposition includes judgment (tasdiq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرف
وليس معنى الحد بهذا الاعتبار معنى المحدود المعقول، لكن إذا لوحظ إلى إبهام أحدهما وقيد بالآخر منضما فيه، ووصف توصيفا لأجل التحصيل والتقويم كان شيئا مؤديا إلى الصورة الوحدانية التي للمحدود كاسبا لها، فالحد علة للمحدود في هذا النحو من الوجود. ومن ههنا ظهر وجه آخر لعدم محمولية الحد في هذا النحو من الوجود.
مثلا الحيوان الناطق في تحديد الإنسان يفهم منه شيء واحد، هو بعينه الحيوان الذي ذلك الحيوان بعينه الناطق، كما أن العقد الحمل يفيد الصورة الاتحادية التي للموضوع مع المحمول في الخارج، إلا أن هناك تركيبا خبريا، ففيه حكم، فيصح السكوت، وهنا تركيب تقييدي، يفيد تصور الاتحاد فقط، فمجموع التصورات المتعلقة بالأجزاء تفصيلا هو الحد الموصل إلى التصور الواحد المتعلق بجميع الأجزاء إجمالا، وهو المحدود.
Chapter on the definition. And the meaning of the definition in this consideration is not the meaning of the defined as understood, but when one observes the ambiguity of one of them and restricts it by the other, included in it, and describes it with a description for the sake of acquisition and rectification, it becomes something leading to the unitary form belonging to the defined, acquiring it. So the definition is a cause for the defined in this mode of existence. From here another aspect appears for the non-predicability of the definition in this mode of existence. For example, 'rational animal' in the definition of 'human' is understood as one thing, which is precisely the animal that is the rational animal itself, just as the predicative proposition yields the unitive form of the subject and predicate in reality, except that there is a predicative composition, so there is a judgment, so silence is permissible, and here there is a restrictive composition, which yields only the image of union. So the totality of the images pertaining to the parts in detail is the definition leading to the single image pertaining to all parts in summary, and that is the defined.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of the definition (hadd) and its relation to the defined (mahdud). It begins by stating that the meaning of the definition is not identical to the meaning of the defined as understood; rather, when the definition is composed with the intention of specifying and rectifying the undefined, it becomes a means to attain the unitary image of the defined. The author then explains that the definition serves as a cause for the defined in this mode of existence, and from this it becomes clear why the definition is not predicated of the defined. The example of 'rational animal' defining 'human' is given: the definition's parts, when combined, produce a single concept that is exactly the defined. This is compared to a predicative proposition (like 'Zayd is standing') which also yields a unitive image but includes a judgment (tasdiq). In contrast, the definition is a restrictive composition (tarkib taqyidi) that only gives a conceptual image (tasawwur) of union. The passage concludes that the detailed images of the parts collectively constitute the definition, and their synthesis yields the single image of the defined in summary. This distinction is crucial in Islamic logic, as it highlights that the definition is not merely a list of terms but a structured unity that introduces the essence.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): definition; composite of genus and differentia that leads to the conceptual image of the defined essence.
المحدود (al-mahdud): the defined; the essence or concept being defined.
التصور (al-tasawwur): conceptual image; here it is the result of definition.
التركيب التقييدي (al-tarkib al-taqyidi): restrictive composition; the linguistic structure in definition that restricts the meaning.

Checkpoint

A) Two separate images: one of animal and one of rational.
B) A single unified image of human that is different from the parts.
C) A judgment that human is rational animal.
D) Only the image of the words 'rational animal'.

Key Takeaway
The definition is a composite structure that causally produces a single conceptual image of the defined essence.

Refuting the Denial of Knowledge Acquisition through Definition
Author refutes later scholars who claim that definition only yields an image of itself, not of the defined

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three logical consequences that follow from the claim that definition does not provide new knowledge of the defined, and explain why they are problematic.

Core Idea
If a definition only gives its own image, the entire purpose of definition as a tool for acquiring new concepts collapses.

This lesson examines a controversy in the Islamic logical tradition: some later scholars argued that definition does not supply a new image of the defined. We will dissect the three consequences the author draws from that view and see why they are unacceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing view
Locate in the Arabic the statement of the later scholars' position: 'no image of the defined is obtained; only the definition's image is obtained essentially.'
2
List the three consequences
Find the three 'لزوم' (necessary implications) the author lists: (1) no acquisition of new concepts, (2) impossibility of acquiring a theoretical from a theoretical, (3) attention to a non-existent.
These are reductio ad absurdum arguments.
3
Explain why each consequence is absurd
For each consequence, articulate why it contradicts the purpose of definition. For example, if definition does not lead to the unknown, it fails as a tool for learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب بعض أجلة المتأخرين إلى أن في التحديد لا يحصل صورة المحدود، بل هناك تصور واحد بالذات للحد، وبالعرض للمحدود، والالتفات بالذات إلى المحدود. ويلزم عليه أولا: عدم تحقق الاكتساب في التصورات بعدم التأدية إلى مجهول حينئذ، وعدم تحقق انتقال ثان من المبادئ إلى المطالب. وثانيا: عدم جواز اكتساب نظري من نظري، وإلا يلزم كون شيء واحد حاصلا بالذات، وغير حاصل، وثالثا: لزوم تعلق الالتفات بالذات إلى أمر معدوم فتأمل فيه.
فإذن الحق ما ذهب إليه الشيخ الرئيس وغيره من المحققين، من حصول صورة المحدود مغايرة لصورة الحد وقت التحديد، كما ينبه عليه المصنف، فقد ظهر أن انكشاف المحدود إنما هو بالصورة المجملة، لا بصورة الحد، وأن الحد في التصور بالكنه ليس مرآة لملاحظة ذي الكنه، لكن بل يحصل هو بنفسه، فقد بان أن العلم بالكنه وبكنه الشيء ليس بينهما فرق حقيقة في نحو الإدراك، فإذن العدول عن اصطلاح القدماء ليس في محله.
قد يحصل كنه الشيء بعد حصول صورة الحد، وقد يحصل أولا نعم، من غير حصولها، ولا يجدي تغايرهما حقيقة في نحو الإدراك.
واعلم: أنه قد اشتهر في أفواه بعض الناس أن العلم بالكنه مختص بالنظريات، وهو ليس بشيء؛ فإن النظر ما يحصل المحدود بالحركة الفكرية، لا ما يحصل صورة الحد، ومن الجائز أن يحصل الحد دفعة مرتبا، ثم يحصل المطلوب المحدود كذلك، كما في القضايا الحدسية، هذا، والله أعلم.
And some of the esteemed later scholars went to the view that in definition, no image of the defined is obtained; rather, there is only one image essentially for the definition, and accidentally for the defined, and attention is essentially to the defined. And it follows from this: first, the non-occurrence of acquisition in conceptual images due to not leading to an unknown at that time, and the non-occurrence of a second transition from principles to aims. Second, the impermissibility of acquiring a theoretical from a theoretical, otherwise it would entail that one thing is essentially obtained and not obtained. Third, the necessity of attention essentially to a non-existent thing. So consider. So then the truth is what the Chief Master (Ibn Sina) and other investigators held: the image of the defined occurs distinct from the image of the definition at the time of definition, as the author alerts. So it has become apparent that the disclosure of the defined is only through the summary image, not through the image of the definition, and that the definition in essential conceptualization is not a mirror for observing the essence-bearer, but rather it itself is obtained. So it became clear that knowledge of the essence and knowledge of the thing's essence have no real difference in the mode of perception. So then the deviation from the terminology of the ancients is not in its place. Sometimes the essence of a thing is obtained after obtaining the image of the definition, and sometimes it is obtained first, yes, without its occurrence, and their real difference does not avail in the mode of perception. And know: it has become famous among some people that knowledge of the essence is specific to theoretical matters, and it is not anything; for theoretical reasoning is what obtains the defined through intellectual movement, not what obtains the image of the definition, and it is possible that the definition is obtained all at once arranged, then the sought defined is obtained similarly, as in intuitive propositions. This, and God knows best.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of an opposing view in the philosophy of definition. Some later scholars held that in the process of definition, no new image of the defined is acquired; rather, the definition gives only its own image, and the defined is known accidentally. The author lists three consequences of this view: (1) there would be no real acquisition of new concepts, since the definition does not lead to the unknown; (2) it would be impossible to acquire a theoretical concept from another theoretical concept, leading to a contradiction; (3) attention would be directed to something non-existent. After presenting these criticisms, the author asserts the correct position held by Ibn Sina: the image of the defined is distinct from the image of the definition and is acquired through the definition. The author then elaborates that the definition's role is to provide the summary image of the defined, not to serve as a mirror to it. He further clarifies that knowledge of the essence (ilm bil-kunh) is not different in kind from the conceptual image obtained. The passage concludes with a note about intuitive (hudusi) vs. discursive knowledge, emphasizing that the definition can be obtained instantly in some cases. All examples in this commentary are drawn from the Islamic logical tradition, such as the definition of 'human' as 'rational animal'.

الشيخ الرئيس
الاكتساب
النظريات
الحدسيات

A) No acquisition of new concepts occurs.
B) The definition becomes useless.
C) The defined becomes unknown.
D) There is no difference between definition and defined.

Key Takeaway
The later scholars' view that definition does not provide new knowledge leads to logical absurdities; the correct view is that definition produces a distinct image of the defined.

Ibn Sina's Solution: Definition as Acquisition of the Essence
Author refutes later scholars who claim that definition only yields an image of itself, not of the defined

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Sina's position that the image of the defined is distinct from the image of the definition, and how this resolves the epistemological problem raised by the later scholars.

Core Idea
Ibn Sina holds that definition is not a mirror but a direct acquisition of the defined's image.

This lesson presents the positive doctrine attributed to Ibn Sina and other investigators. After refuting the opposing view, the author clarifies the true role of definition: it provides a distinct image of the defined, not merely its own repetition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the statement of the truth
Find in the Arabic the phrase 'فإذن الحق ما ذهب إليه الشيخ الرئيس' which introduces Ibn Sina's correct view.
2
Identify the claim of distinct images
Note that the author asserts 'حصول صورة المحدود مغايرة لصورة الحد' – the image of the defined is distinct from the image of the definition.
This is the core epistemological claim.
3
Understand the role of the summary image
The author states that disclosure of the defined is through the 'summary image' (صورة مجملة), not through the definition's image. The definition triggers the acquisition of a new concept.
4
Grasp the mode of perception
The author argues that knowledge of the essence (علم بالكنه) and the conceptual image are not different in mode of perception. The definition itself can be obtained either instantaneously or through reasoning.

The Objection Against Definition and Its Response
Author presents the objection and response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the two-pronged objection against definition and evaluate the validity of the response using the concept of i'tibar (consideration).

Core Idea
Definition is not tautology: essential identity with conceptual difference.

This lesson unpacks a classic objection in Islamic logic: definition (ta'rif) seems either redundant or impossible. We will examine the objection and the subtle response that saves definition by distinguishing between essential identity and conceptual consideration (i'tibar). This is a foundational move in understanding how definitions yield new knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection's two horns
The objection argues that definition must be either by essence (or all parts) or by accidents. If by essence, it is tautological (tahsil al-hasil). If by accidents, it cannot give knowledge of the true essence (kunh). Locate both in the Arabic: 'فالتعريف تحصيل الحاصل' and 'والعوارض لا تعطيه'.
The phrase 'تحصيل الحاصل' is key: obtaining what is already obtained.
2
Understand the consequence: both hadd and rasm are invalid
The objection concludes that all forms of definition (hadd and rasm) are invalid because they fall into one of the two traps. Find the sentence: 'فالأقسام ... بأسرها باطلة'.
3
Analyze the response: the concept of i'tibar
The response (wajh al-daf') concedes that the definition is identical in essence (dhat) but different in consideration (i'tibar). This means the arrangement of parts provides new conceptual knowledge. Find 'مغاير بالاعتبار'.
'I'tibar' is a crucial term: it means a mental perspective or consideration.
4
Assess the response: does it solve the objection?
Consider whether distinguishing essential identity from conceptual consideration truly avoids tahsil al-hasil. The response claims that obtaining the definition is 'تحصيل غير الحاصل' (obtaining what is not already obtained). Evaluate this move.
This step requires critical thinking: does the response actually refute the objection, or does it shift the burden?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرف بِنَفْسِهَا أَوْ بِجَمِيعِ أَجْزَائِهَا ، وَهُوَ نَفْسُهَا ، فَالتَّعْرِيفُ تَحْصِيلُ الْحَاصِلِ، وهو باطل، أَوْ بِالْعَوَارِض ، وَلَا عِلْمَ  بِالْحَقِيقَةِ إِلَّا الْعِلْمُ بِالْكُنْهِ، وَالْعَوارض لا تُعْطِيهِ، فقد بطل التعريف بالعوارض ، فَالْأَقْسَامُ، أي أقسام التعريف التي هي الحد والرسم بِأَسْرِهَا بَاطِلَةٌ . وجه الدفع : أنا نختار أن التعريف بجميع أجزائها، وهو نفسها بالذات مغایر بالاعتبار ، فتحصيلها تحصيل غير الحاصل.
Chapter on the definition: it is either by itself or by all its parts, and it is itself, so the definition is obtaining what is already obtained, and it is invalid; or by accidents, and there is no knowledge of the essence except knowledge of the intrinsic nature, and accidents do not give it, so definition by accidents is invalid. Thus the sections, i.e., the sections of definition which are the limit and the sketch, all are invalid. The response: We choose that definition by all its parts, and it is identical in essence but different in consideration, so obtaining it is obtaining what is not already obtained.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents the classical objection against definition (ta'rif) as a means of acquiring new knowledge. The objection is twofold: firstly, if the definition is by the thing's essence (dhat) or by all its parts, then the definition is merely a repetition of the thing itself, resulting in 'tahsil al-hasil' (obtaining what is already obtained) which is futile. Secondly, if the definition is by accidents (a'warid), then it cannot grant knowledge of the true essence (haqiqah) because accidents are external to the intrinsic nature (kunh). Consequently, both types of definition—the limit (hadd) and the sketch (rasm)—are invalid. The response (wajh al-daf') counters that definition by all parts is identical in essence (dhat) but different in consideration (i'tibar). The detailed arrangement of the parts produces a new mental conception that was not present in the initial vague idea, thereby avoiding tautology. This response preserves the utility of definition while acknowledging the objection.

Key Terms
التعريف
الحد
الرسم
تحصيل الحاصل
وجه الدفع

A) Because the definition is not identical to the thing at all
B) Because the thing is unknown before definition
C) Because although identical in essence, it is different in consideration (i'tibar)
D) Because the definition uses accidents, not essence

Key Takeaway
The objection that definition is either tautological or impossible is countered by the insight that definition provides new conceptual knowledge through arrangement, even if the essence is the same.

Hadd and Rasm

6 min
The Imam's Consequence: All Conceptions Are Self-Evident
Author discusses the consequence that all conceptions are self-evident due to invalid definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the logical consequence that if definition fails to produce new conceptions, then all conceptions must be self-evident, and identify the role of this argument in Islamic epistemology.

Core Idea
If definition cannot generate new knowledge of concepts, then all concepts are innate.

In this passage, the author draws a striking conclusion from the earlier critique of definition: if definition (ta'rif) cannot actually produce new conceptions (tasawwurat), then all conceptions must already be present in the mind from the start—they are self-evident (badihiyyah). This position is attributed to the Imam (Fakhr al-Din al-Razi). Understanding this move is crucial for grasping the debate over whether all knowledge is acquired or some is innate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the premise
The author states that definition is invalid as a way of acquiring conceptions. Locate the phrase 'بطلان التعريف الذي هو طريق اكتساب التصورات' in the Arabic.
This premise is assumed from the previous discussion.
2
State the conclusion
The conclusion is that all conceptions are self-evident (بداهة التصورات كلها). See the Arabic: 'ذَهَبَ الْإِمَامُ إِلَى بَدَاهَةِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ كُلِّهَا'.
This is a direct implication: if there is no valid way to acquire a conception, then it must be already known.
3
Analyze the logical connection
The reasoning is: if definition is the only way to acquire new conceptions, and definition is invalid, then no conception can be acquired. Therefore, every conception must be innate (self-evident). This is a form of argument by elimination.
This conclusion is radical and leads to further problems.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider what it means for all conceptions to be self-evident. Does this include complex concepts? How would this affect the possibility of learning? This is a controversial position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْ هَهُنَا، أي لأجل بطلان التعريف الذي هو طريق اكتساب التصورات ذَهَبَ الإمام إِلَى بَدَاهَةِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ كُلِّهَا. هذا كله في التحديد، وأما في الرسم فالأمر مشكل ; لأن صورة المرسوم المغايرة لصورة الرسم ينقبض عن حصولها العقل، وإن جوزه الأكثرون ; إذ لا يبقى إذن فرق بين التحديد والترسيم، وإذا لم يحصل صورة أخرى لم يتحقق حصول مجهول، ولا الحركة الثانية ، إلا أن يقال : الصورة الوحدانية المجملة المركبة من العوارض تحصل بعد حصول الرسم، وتفيد الامتياز عما عداه.
And from here, i.e., due to the invalidity of definition which is the way of acquiring conceptions, the Imam went to the view that all conceptions are self-evident. This all is concerning the limit. As for the sketch, the matter is problematic, because the image of the defined thing which is different from the image of the sketch, the mind shrinks from obtaining it, even though the majority permit it. For then there would be no difference between limit and sketching, and if no other image is obtained, then obtaining an unknown is not realized, nor the second movement, unless it is said: the unitary holistic image composed of accidents is obtained after obtaining the sketch, and it gives distinction from others.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage draws a consequence from the earlier critique of definition: if definition (ta'rif) is invalid as a means of acquiring new conceptions (tasawwurat), then it follows that all conceptions must be innate (badihiyyah). This is attributed to the Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi). The author then turns to a specific problem with definition by accident (rasm). While the majority of logicians permit rasm, the author finds it problematic because the mental image of the defined thing (mursam) is different from the image of the definition (rasm), and the mind may be unable to combine them into a new distinct image. If no new image results, then no unknown is acquired, and there is no 'second movement' (al-harakat al-thaniyyah) from potential to actual knowledge. However, a possible solution is that after the rasm, a holistic unitary image composed of the accidents is obtained, which provides distinction from other things. This preserves the utility of rasm.

Key Terms
البداهة
التصورات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what led the Imam to conclude that all conceptions are self-evident?
A) The validity of definition
B) The invalidity of definition as a way to acquire conceptions
C) The majority's opinion on rasm
D) The existence of the second movement

Key Takeaway
The invalidity of definition forces the radical conclusion that all conceptions are innate and not acquired.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a brief argument: If all conceptions are self-evident, then explain how new knowledge (like learning a language) is possible. Does the author's position allow for any acquisition? Use the passage to support your answer.

Hadd and Rasm

The Problem with Definition by Accident (Rasm)
Author discusses the problem with rasm and the difficulty of obtaining a new image.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the problem with rasm (definition by accident) regarding the acquisition of a new mental image, and evaluate the proposed solution.

Core Idea
Rasm fails to produce a new distinct image because the mind cannot combine the accidental properties into a unique essence.

After discussing the invalidity of definition by essence (hadd), the author turns to definition by accident (rasm). Even if rasm is permitted by the majority, the author finds a serious difficulty: the image of the thing defined (mursam) is different from the image of the definition (rasm), and the mind may be unable to grasp a new distinct image from the accidents. This threatens the very purpose of definition: to acquire new knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two images
The author distinguishes between 'صورة المرسوم' (image of the defined thing) and 'صورة الرسم' (image of the sketch/definition). The first is the mental representation of the thing itself, the second is the set of accidental properties used to define it.
The problem is that these two images are different, and the mind must somehow connect them.
2
Identify the difficulty
The author says 'ينقبض عن حصولها العقل' – the mind shrinks from obtaining the image of the defined thing from the sketch. In other words, the mind cannot automatically derive the essence from accidents.
This is why rasm is problematic: it doesn't guarantee a new conception.
3
Understand the consequence
If no new image is obtained, then no unknown (مجهول) is acquired, and the 'second movement' (الحركة الثانية) from potential to actual knowledge does not occur. Definition loses its purpose.
The second movement is the cognitive transition from ignorance to knowledge.
4
Examine the proposed solution
The author mentions a possible counter: 'الصورة الوحدانية المجملة المركبة من العوارض' – a unitary holistic image composed of accidents is obtained after the rasm, and it provides distinction from other things. This might save rasm.
This solution is not fully endorsed; it is presented as a possible response from the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْ هَهُنَا، أي لأجل بطلان التعريف الذي هو طريق اكتساب التصورات ذَهَبَ الإمام إِلَى بَدَاهَةِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ كُلِّهَا. هذا كله في التحديد، وأما في الرسم فالأمر مشكل ; لأن صورة المرسوم المغايرة لصورة الرسم ينقبض عن حصولها العقل، وإن جوزه الأكثرون ; إذ لا يبقى إذن فرق بين التحديد والترسيم، وإذا لم يحصل صورة أخرى لم يتحقق حصول مجهول، ولا الحركة الثانية ، إلا أن يقال : الصورة الوحدانية المجملة المركبة من العوارض تحصل بعد حصول الرسم، وتفيد الامتياز عما عداه.
And from here, i.e., due to the invalidity of definition which is the way of acquiring conceptions, the Imam went to the view that all conceptions are self-evident. This all is concerning the limit. As for the sketch, the matter is problematic, because the image of the defined thing which is different from the image of the sketch, the mind shrinks from obtaining it, even though the majority permit it. For then there would be no difference between limit and sketching, and if no other image is obtained, then obtaining an unknown is not realized, nor the second movement, unless it is said: the unitary holistic image composed of accidents is obtained after obtaining the sketch, and it gives distinction from others.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage draws a consequence from the earlier critique of definition: if definition (ta'rif) is invalid as a means of acquiring new conceptions (tasawwurat), then it follows that all conceptions must be innate (badihiyyah). This is attributed to the Imam (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi). The author then turns to a specific problem with definition by accident (rasm). While the majority of logicians permit rasm, the author finds it problematic because the mental image of the defined thing (mursam) is different from the image of the definition (rasm), and the mind may be unable to combine them into a new distinct image. If no new image results, then no unknown is acquired, and there is no 'second movement' (al-harakat al-thaniyyah) from potential to actual knowledge. However, a possible solution is that after the rasm, a holistic unitary image composed of the accidents is obtained, which provides distinction from other things. This preserves the utility of rasm.

Key Terms

الحركة الثانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main problem with rasm?
A) It is too long
B) The mind cannot obtain a new image of the defined thing from the accidental description
C) It is not permitted by the majority
D) It does not provide distinction from other things

Key Takeaway
Rasm is problematic because it may fail to generate a new mental image, undermining its purpose as a means of acquiring knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given a definition of 'wine' as 'an intoxicating beverage made from grapes', identify whether this is a hadd or rasm. Then, evaluate whether this definition would face the problem raised in the passage: does it produce a new mental image distinct from the image of the definition itself?

The Verbal Definition as a Conceptual Demand
Author argues verbal definition is a conceptual demand, not a judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining characteristic of a verbal definition and distinguish it from a judgment, using the example of 'ghadanfar' and 'lion'.

Core Idea
Verbal definition answers 'what is it?' without judgment.

In this passage, the author classifies verbal definition as a conceptual demand. He explains that when we define a word like 'ghadanfar' as 'lion', we are not making a judgment about existence, but simply presenting a concept. This distinction is crucial for understanding the role of definition in the Islamic logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
Find the sentence where the author states that verbal definition is a conceptual demand. Notice how he aligns with the view of al-Sa'd.
The claim is: 'التعريف اللفظي من المطالب التصورية'
2
Analyze the example
Consider the exchange: 'ghadanfar exists' followed by 'what is ghadanfar?' Explanatory definition as 'lion'. Observe that no judgment is made.
The author says 'فليس هناك حكم. بل إحضار صورة'
3
Distinguish from judgment
Contrast this definition with a proposition that involves a judgment. In a judgment, affirmation or denial occurs. Here, only the concept is presented.
Verbal definitions are conceptual, not assertoric.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم
اليقين، وناقص وهو [الــظن، وتخالفهما نوعي، على رأي من يرى التخالف بالشدة نوعيا أو صنفي على رأي غيره والتصور منه تعقل، وهو تام ينكشف به حقيقة الشيء، وناقص به يمتاز المعلوم والكاسب والمكتسب والتصوري والنظري العلم فإذا أريد تحصيل نظري فربما يتصور أجزاؤه، فيحصل في الذهن أشباحها ولوحظت وقيدت كما ذكرنا، فيحصل بعد ذلك شبح المطلوب، فينكشف به حقيقته، وربما يتصور العوارض، فيحصل أشباحها ويحصل بعد ذلك شبح به يمتاز المطلوب امتيازا تاما، كما في الرسوم المتساوية، أو ناقصا، كما في الرسوم العامة أو الخاصة.
هذا وإن كان مخالفا للجمهور، لكنه لعله يخالف التحقيق، وأما بعد تسلیم اتحاد العلم والمعلوم فيختل أمر التعريفات اختلالا فاحشا؛ فإن حصول صورة مغايرة للحد والرسم مما يمجه الطبع السليم.
العلم.
فإن قلت: فما تصنع لدلائل الوجود الذهني؟
قلت: لو سلمت فلا تنتج إلا أن للأشياء وجودا ذهنيا، لا أنه هو
فإن قلت: فهذا جمع بين المذهبين مذهب الشبح ومذهب حصول الصورة؟
قلت: أي فساد في ذلك؟ إنما الفساد لو قيل إن الشبح والصورة كلاهما علمان ومبدء ان للانكشاف، ونحن لا نقول به، بل إن المعلوم لا ينكشف إلا بالشبح، وحصول المعلوم لا يحتاج إليه إلا لأن العلم صفة ذات إضافة، فلا بد له من متعلق، وإذ ليس في الخارج ففي الذهن، ثم اتحاد العلم مع المعلوم مما يبطل الاشتراك المعنوي للعلم كما أشير إليه في أوائل الكتاب فتأمل وتثبت هذا، والله أعلم بالصواب.
(الثَّانِي: التَّعْرِيفُ اللَّفْظِيُّ منَ المطالب التصورية؛ فَإِنَّهُ جواب وكا، اختيار المصنف لرأي السعد في أن التعريف ألا ترى إذا قلنا الغضنفر موجود. فقال مَا هُوَ جَوَابُ مَا فَهُوَ تَصَوُّرٌ الْمُخَاطَبُ مَا الْغَضَفَرُ؟ فَفَسَّرْنَاهُ بِالْأسد، فليس هناك حكم. بل إحضار صورة.
فإن قلت: المطالب التصورية يطلب بها صورة غير حاصلة؟
قلت: بل يطلب الأعم منه ومن الإحضار، فتأمل فيه.
فإن قلت: إذا خوطب من حضر عنده صورة الأسد، سد، وقيل الغضنفر)
Commentary on Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum: Certainty, and incomplete which is [opinion], and their difference is specific, according to the view that sees difference by intensity as specific or generic according to others. And conception from it is intellection, and it is complete, by which the reality of the thing is disclosed, and incomplete by which the known is distinguished. And the acquisitive and the acquired, and the conceptual and the theoretical knowledge. So if one intends to obtain a theoretical [concept], perhaps he conceives its parts, so their phantoms occur in the mind, and they are observed and restricted as we mentioned, then after that the phantom of the sought occurs, so its reality is disclosed by it. And perhaps he conceives the accidental attributes, so their phantoms occur and after that occurs a phantom by which the sought is distinguished completely, as in equal descriptions, or incompletely, as in general or specific descriptions. This, although it contradicts the majority, yet perhaps it contradicts verification. And after granting the unity of knowledge and the known, the matter of definitions becomes extremely corrupted; for the occurrence of an image different from the definition and description is rejected by sound nature. Knowledge. If you say: What do you do with the proofs of mental existence? I say: Even if granted, they only prove that things have mental existence, not that it is the same. If you say: This is a combination of the two doctrines: the doctrine of the phantom and the doctrine of the occurrence of the image? I say: What corruption is in that? The corruption would only be if it were said that the phantom and the image are both knowledges and principles of disclosure, which we do not say. Rather, the known is only disclosed by the phantom, and the occurrence of the known does not need it except because knowledge is an attribute that has a relation, so it must have a relation; and since it is not in the external, [it is] in the mind. Then the unity of knowledge with the known invalidates the homonymy of knowledge as alluded to in the beginning of the book. So ponder and be certain of this, and Allah knows best. (Second: The verbal definition is among the conceptual demands; for it is the answer to 'what'? The author's choice of the view of al-Sa'd is that the definition: Do you not see that if we say 'al-ghadanfar exists', and he asks 'what is the answer to what?' So it is a conception of the addressee: 'What is al-ghadanfar?' So we interpreted it as lion; there is no judgment, but rather a presentation of an image. If you say: The conceptual demands seek an image that is not present? I say: Rather it seeks the more general than that and than presentation, so reflect on it. If you say: If someone is addressed in whose presence the image of a lion is present, and it is said 'al-ghadanfar'? ...)
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of verbal definition and its classification as a conceptual demand. The author begins by discussing the nature of certainty and opinion, and the distinction between complete and incomplete conception. He describes how theoretical knowledge proceeds by forming phantoms of parts and then the whole. He then addresses an objection: if knowledge and the known are one, then definitions are corrupted. He argues that mental existence is proven but not that the mental image is identical to knowledge. He distinguishes his view from those who say both phantom and image are knowledge. Then he turns to verbal definition: it is a conceptual demand because it answers 'what is it?' without a judgment. He gives the example of explaining 'ghadanfar' as 'lion' – this is purely conception, not a judgment. He responds to an objection that conceptual demands seek an absent image, by saying they seek a more general notion including presentation. The passage defends the view of al-Sa'd that verbal definition is a conceptual demand.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
المطلب التصوري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does a verbal definition (التعريف اللفظي) do?
A) It gives a judgment about the existence of the defined thing.
B) It presents the concept of the defined thing without any judgment.
C) It provides a complete description including all accidents.
D) It combines both concept and judgment.

Key Takeaway
A verbal definition is a conceptual demand that answers 'what is it?' without any judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Use the example of 'ghadanfar' to practice identifying verbal definitions. Find another term from Islamic law (e.g., 'riba') and formulate a verbal definition that only presents the concept, without any judgment.

The Role of the Phantom in Conception
Author argues verbal definition is a conceptual demand, not a judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the phantom (shabah) functions in disclosure and distinguish between complete and incomplete conception.

Core Idea
The phantom is the mental form that either discloses reality or distinguishes the known.

The author presents a theory of conception where the mind forms phantoms of parts and then of the whole. These phantoms lead to disclosure of the thing's reality or a distinguishing feature. This theory underlies the cognitive process behind verbal definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two kinds of conception
Find where the author distinguishes complete conception (discloses reality) and incomplete conception (distinguishes the known).
Complete: 'ينكشف به حقيقة الشيء', incomplete: 'به يمتاز المعلوم'
2
Trace the formation of phantoms
Notice how the author describes that when seeking a theoretical concept, the parts are conceived first, their phantoms occur, then the phantom of the sought occurs.
The process: parts → phantoms → observation → restriction → phantom of sought
3
Contrast with accidental attributes
Sometimes one conceives the accidental attributes, leading to a phantom that distinguishes the sought completely (as in equal descriptions) or incompletely (as in general/specific descriptions).
This relates to the distinction between complete and incomplete definitions (had vs rasm).

Source Text

If you say: This is a combination of the two doctrines: the doctrine of the phantom and the doctrine of the occurrence of the image? I say: What corruption is in that? The corruption would only be if it were said that the phantom and the image are both knowledges and principles of disclosure, which we do not say. Rather, the known is only disclosed by the phantom, and the occurrence of the known does not need it except because knowledge is an attribute that has a relation, so it must have a relation; and since it is not in the external, [it is] in the mind. Then the unity of knowledge with the known invalidates the homonymy of knowledge as alluded to in the beginning of the book. So ponder and be certain of this, and Allah knows best. (Second: The verbal definition is among the conceptual demands; for it is the answer to 'what'? The author's choice of the view of al-Sa'd is that the definition: Do you not see that if we say 'al-ghadanfar exists', and he asks 'what is the answer to what?' So it is a conception of the addressee: 'What is al-ghadanfar?' So we interpreted it as lion; there is no judgment, but rather a presentation of an image. If you say: The conceptual demands seek an image that is not present? I say: Rather it seeks the more general than that and than presentation, so reflect on it. If you say: If someone is addressed in whose presence the image of a lion is present, and it is said 'al-ghadanfar'? ...)
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of verbal definition and its classification as a conceptual demand. The author begins by discussing the nature of certainty and opinion, and the distinction between complete and incomplete conception. He describes how theoretical knowledge proceeds by forming phantoms of parts and then the whole. He then addresses an objection: if knowledge and the known are one, then definitions are corrupted. He argues that mental existence is proven but not that the mental image is identical to knowledge. He distinguishes his view from those who say both phantom and image are knowledge. Then he turns to verbal definition: it is a conceptual demand because it answers 'what is it?' without a judgment. He gives the example of explaining 'ghadanfar' as 'lion' – this is purely conception, not a judgment. He responds to an objection that conceptual demands seek an absent image, by saying they seek a more general notion including presentation. The passage defends the view of al-Sa'd that verbal definition is a conceptual demand.

Phantoms are mental forms that either disclose reality or distinguish the known, forming the basis of conception.
