Abstractive Attribution and Its Conditions
Definition and objection resolution for abstractive attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define abstractive attribution, distinguish it from conjunctive attribution, and explain the logical objection and its resolution regarding the existence of the attribute in the locus of attribution.

Core Idea
Abstractive attribution does not require the attribute to exist in the same locus as the subject—only the subject's existence is needed.

In this passage from Bahr al-Ulum, the author defines a crucial distinction in logical predication: the difference between conjunctive attribution (where attribute and subject coexist externally) and abstractive attribution (where the attribute is mentally extracted). This distinction becomes essential when analyzing objections about whether a relation (nisba) requires the existence of both relata. The objection and its resolution hinge on differentiating between the essence of attribution and its existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of attribution
Locate the definitions of conjunctive (inḍimāmī) and abstractive (intizāʿī) attribution in the passage. Note that conjunctive attribution requires the attribute to inhere in the subject externally (e.g., 'body is white'), while abstractive attribution involves mental extraction (e.g., 'sky is above').
The passage begins by contrasting abstractive with conjunctive.
2
Understand the condition for the attribute's existence
The text states that absolute attribution does not require the attribute's existence in the locus of attribution, only the subject's existence. However, the attribute must exist somewhere (mind or external world) absolutely.
This is the core difference between the two types.
3
Recognize the objection
The objection: Attribution is a relation (nisba), and a relation requires the existence of both relata (subject and attribute). Therefore, the attribute must exist in the same locus as the subject. Find where this objection is raised in the passage.
The objection is introduced after the initial definitions.
4
Understand the resolution: essence vs. existence of attribution
The resolution, attributed to al-Sayyid al-Jurjani and al-Dawani, distinguishes between the essence of attribution (nafs al-ittiṣāf) and its existence (wujūd al-ittiṣāf). The essence of attribution is external (the relation itself), but its existence is mental. Only the existence requires both relata to be realized externally.
This resolves the objection without requiring the attribute's physical coexistence.
5
Apply to the examples given
The passage provides examples: For conjunctive, body and whiteness are united externally; for abstractive, sky and above-ness are separate externally but related in the mind. Confirm that in abstractive attribution, the attribute (above-ness) does not exist in the sky externally—it is mentally extracted from the relation.
These examples solidify the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(بِخِلَافِ) الاتصاف (الاِنْتِزَاعِيُّ)، وهو ما كان بانتزاع الصفة؛ فإنه لا يستدعي وجودهما في ظرف الاتصاف، بل (يَسْتَدْعِي تُبُوتَ الْمَوْصُوفِ فَقَطْ، فَمُطْلَقُ الاِتِّصَافِ الشامل للانضمامي والانتزاعي (لَا يَسْتَدْعِي ثُبُوتَ الصَّفَةِ ظَرْفِهِ) ، أي ظرف الاتصاف، بل ثبوت الموصوف، (أَمَّا مُطْلَقُ النُّبُوتِ)، أي ثبوت الصفة، سواء كان في الذهن أو في الخارج (فَضَرُورِيُّ) في مطلق الاتصاف؛ فَإِنَّ مَا لَا يَكُونَ مَوْجُودًا يَكُونَ مَوْجُودًا فِي نَفْسِهِ يَسْتَحِيلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَوْجُودًا لِشَيْءٍ)، هذا ليس ضروريا ولا مبرهنا عليه، بل الضرورة شاهدة بأن الوجود الأذهان العالية أو السافلة لغو في اتصاف الموصوف بها. نعم، يجب وجود الصفة في ظرف الاتصاف بوجود المنشأ، وإلا صارت اختراعية. ثم ههنا إشكال، وهو: أن الاتصاف نسبة وهي فرع وجود المنتسبين، فلا بد من وجود الصفة في ظرفه أجاب عنه السيد المحقق قدس سره وتبعه المحقق الدواني أنه فرق بين نفس الاتصاف ووجود الاتصاف، وههنا في الخارج نفس الاتصاف، والمستدعي لوجود المنتسبين هو الثاني فقط . ووهم صاحب الأفق المبين أن كون نفس الشيء في ظرف مع عدم تحقق وجوده غير معقول؛ فإن الوجود هو الكون، ورجع عن الطريقة القويمة القديمة، وتبعه المصنف وقال: (وَالاتِّصَافُ لَيْسَ مُتَحَقِّقًا فِي الْخَارِجِ، حَتَّى يَلْزَمَ تَحَقُّقُ الصَّفَةِ فِيهِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ نِسْبَةٌ، وَكُلُّ نِسْبَةٍ تَحَقُّقُهَا فَرْعُ تَحَقُّقِ الْمُنْتَسِبَيْنِ، بَلْ هُوَ مُتَحَقِّقٌ في الذِّهْنِ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الإِنْضِمَامِيِّ الْخَارِجِيِّ الْمَوْصُوفُ مُتَحِدًا مَعَ الصِّفَةِ فِي الْأَعْيَانِ، كَالْجِسْمِ وَالْأَبْيَضِ، وَفِي الانْتِزَاعِيِّ الْخَارِجِيِّ مُنْحِدًا بِحَسَبِ الْأَعْيَانِ، كَالسَّمَاءِ وَالْفَوْقِيَّةِ).
Contrary to abstractive attribution, which is by extraction of the attribute; for it does not require their existence in the locus of attribution, but only requires the existence of the subject. So absolute attribution, which includes conjunctive and abstractive, does not require the existence of the attribute in its locus, i.e., the locus of attribution, but only the existence of the subject. As for absolute existence, i.e., the existence of the attribute, whether in the mind or externally, it is necessary in absolute attribution. For that which does not exist cannot be existent in itself; it is impossible for it to be existent for something. This is neither necessary nor demonstrable, rather necessity testifies that existence in high or low minds is futile in the attribution of the subject to it. Yes, the existence of the attribute is required in the locus of attribution through the existence of the source, otherwise it becomes invented. Then here is an objection: that attribution is a relation, and a relation is a branch of the existence of the two relata, so the existence of the attribute in its locus is unavoidable. Al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq, may his secret be sanctified, answered it, followed by al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani, that there is a distinction between the essence of attribution and the existence of attribution. Here externally is the essence of attribution, and what requires the existence of the two relata is only the second. The author of al-Ufuq mistakenly thought that the existence of a thing itself in a locus without the realization of its existence is unintelligible, for existence is the 'being'. He reverted from the correct ancient method, and the author followed him and said: 'Attribution is not realized externally such that the realization of the attribute in it is necessitated, because it is a relation, and every relation's realization is a branch of the realization of the two relata; rather, it is realized in the mind, even if in external conjunctive attribution the subject is united with the attribute in external entities, like body and whiteness, and in external abstractive attribution it is unified according to external entities, like sky and above-ness.'
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and dialectical exposition from a commentary on al-Sullam. It defines 'abstractive attribution' (al-ittiṣāf al-intizāʿī) as a type of predication where the attribute is mentally extracted (like 'wise' from wisdom) and does not require the attribute to exist in the same locus as the subject. The author contrasts it with 'conjunctive attribution' (al-ittiṣāf al-inḍimāmī) where both subject and attribute coexist externally. The commentary then clarifies that absolute attribution, whether conjunctive or abstractive, does not require the attribute's existence in the locus, but the absolute existence of the attribute is necessary—it must exist somewhere (mind or external world). An objection is raised: attribution is a relation (nisba), and relations depend on the existence of both relata, so the attribute must exist in the same locus as the subject. The response, attributed to al-Sayyid al-Jurjani and al-Dawani, distinguishes between the essence of attribution (nafs al-ittiṣāf) and its existence (wujūd al-ittiṣāf). The essence of attribution can be external (the relation itself) while its existence is mental. The commentator criticizes the author of al-Ufuq for conflating essence and existence, and then quotes the author's conclusion: attribution is not realized externally because it is a relation; relations are mental entities. Examples: body and whiteness are united externally in conjunctive attribution; sky and above-ness are separated externally in abstractive attribution.

Key Terms
اتصاف
انتزاعي
انضمامي
نسبة

Key Takeaway
Abstractive attribution allows predication without physical coexistence of attribute and subject, relying on mental extraction—a key tool for analyzing relational predicates in logic and jurisprudence.

Two Types of Attribution: Conjunctive vs. Derived
Distinguishes two types of attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conjunctive attribution (al-ittisaf al-indimami) and derived attribution (al-ittisaf al-intiza'i) and identify which type is at play in a given example.

Core Idea
Derived attribution needs only the subject; the attribute is mentally extracted.

In Islamic logic, not all attributions are alike. Some require the attribute to be physically present with the subject (conjunctive), while others derive the attribute from the subject’s own state (derived). This distinction is crucial for understanding how predicates relate to subjects in propositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the attributive phrase
Look at the statement. What is being said about the subject? E.g., 'the body is white' or 'the sky is above'.
The attribute is the second term.
2
Check if the attribute exists separately
For conjunctive attribution, the attribute (e.g., whiteness) is a real entity that can join the subject. For derived attribution, the attribute (e.g., above-ness) is not an entity but a relation derived from the subject's position.
If you can point to the attribute as an independent thing, it's likely conjunctive.
3
Apply the test of existence in the locus
Ask: Does the attribute need to exist in the external locus for the statement to be true? For conjunctive, yes (whiteness must be in the body). For derived, no (above-ness does not need to exist in the sky).
The locus (zarf) is the external or mental context.
4
Classify the attribution
Based on the test, determine if it is conjunctive (indimami) or derived (intiza'i).
Derived attribution is sometimes called 'attribution by derivation'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف الاتصاف الانتزاعي، وهو ما كان بانتزاع الصفة؛ فإنه لا يستدعي وجودهما في ظرف الاتصاف، بل يستدعي ثبوت الموصوف فقط. فمطلق الاتصاف الشامل للانضمامي والانتزاعي لا يستدعي ثبوت الصفة في ظرفه، أي ظرف الاتصاف، بل ثبوت الموصوف. أما مطلق الثبوت، أي ثبوت الصفة سواء كان في الذهن أو في الخارج فضروري في مطلق الاتصاف؛ فإن ما لا يكون موجودًا في نفسه يستحيل أن يكون موجودًا لشيء. هذا ليس ضروريًا ولا مبرهنًا عليه، بل الضرورة شاهدة بأن الوجود في الأذهان العالية أو السافلة لغو في اتصاف الموصوف بها. نعم، يجب وجود الصفة في ظرف الاتصاف بوجود المنشأ، وإلا صارت اختراعية. ثم ههنا إشكال، وهو: أن الاتصاف نسبة وهي فرع وجود المنتسبين، فلا بد من وجود الصفة في ظرفه. أجاب عنه السيد المحقق ـ قدس سره ـ وتبعه المحقق الدواني أنه فرق بين نفس الاتصاف ووجود الاتصاف، وههنا في الخارج نفس الاتصاف، والمستدعي لوجود المنتسبين هو الثاني فقط. ووهم صاحب الأفق المبين أن كون نفس الشيء في ظرف مع عدم تحقق وجوده غير معقول؛ فإن الوجود هو الكون، ورجع عن الطريقة القويمة القديمة، وتبعه المصنف وقال: والاتصاف ليس متحققًا في الخارج، حتى يلزم تحقق الصفة فيه؛ لأنه نسبة، وكل نسبة تحققها فرع تحقق المنتسبين، بل هو متحقق في الذهن، وإن كان في الانضمامي الخارجي الموصوف متحدًا مع الصفة في الأعيان، كالجسم والأبيض، وفي الانتزاعي الخارجي منحذًا بحسب الأعيان، كالسماء والفوقية. تبصرة في تحقيق المحصورات اعلم: أن مقصود السيد ـ قدس سره الشريف ـ بتحقق نفس الاتصاف في الخارج تحقق الموصوف بحيث ينتزع منه الصفة، فإن أنكر الواهم هذا المعنى فقد خالف الضرورة، وإلا فتنازعه لفظي. ثم إنه ماذا يقول في الانضمامي الخارجي؟ فإما أن يقول أن نفسه في العين دون وجوده، فقد اعترف الفرق بين تحقق نفس الشيء وتحقق وجوده، أو يقول بتحقق وجوده فيه أيضًا، فمع كونه ضروري البطلان يفضي إلى التسلسل المحال، والله أعلم بالصواب.
Contrary to derived attribution, which is by derivation of the attribute, for it does not require their existence in the locus of attribution, but rather requires only the subsistence of the described. So absolute attribution, which includes conjunctive and derived, does not require the subsistence of the attribute in its locus, i.e., the locus of attribution, but rather the subsistence of the described. As for absolute subsistence, i.e., the subsistence of the attribute, whether in the mind or externally, it is necessary in absolute attribution; for that which does not exist in itself is impossible to exist for something. This is not necessary nor proven, rather necessity witnesses that existence in high or low minds is vain in the attribution of the described to it. Yes, the existence of the attribute in the locus of attribution is required with the existence of the source, otherwise it becomes invented. Then here is a difficulty, which is: attribution is a relation and it is a branch of the existence of the two relata, so the existence of the attribute in its locus is necessary. The chief master, may his secret be sanctified, answered it, followed by the chief al-Dawani, that he distinguished between the very attribution and the existence of the attribution, and here externally is the very attribution, and the requirer of the existence of the two relata is only the second. And the author of 'al-Ufuq al-Mubin' imagined that the very thing being in a locus without the realization of its existence is unintelligible; for existence is the 'being', and he reverted from the sound ancient method, and the author followed him and said: Attribution is not realized externally, so that the realization of the attribute in it would be necessary; because it is a relation, and every relation its realization is a branch of the realization of the two relata, rather it is realized in the mind, even if in the external conjunctive the described is united with the attribute in individuals, like body and white, and in the derived external it is separated according to individuals, like sky and above-ness. An admonition concerning the investigation of quantified propositions: Know that the intention of the master, may his noble secret be sanctified, in the realization of the very attribution externally is the realization of the described such that the attribute is derived from it; if the objector denies this meaning, he has contradicted necessity, otherwise his dispute is verbal. Then what does he say about the external conjunctive? Either he says that its very self is in the external without its existence, so he has admitted the difference between the realization of the very thing and the realization of its existence; or he says that its existence also is realized in it, then while being necessarily false it leads to impossible regress. And God knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of earlier logical positions on the nature of attribution (ittisaf). The commentator begins by distinguishing two types of attribution: derived attribution (al-ittisaf al-intiza'i), which is based on deriving an attribute from a subject (e.g., 'sky is above' where 'above' is derived from the sky's position), and conjunctive attribution (al-ittisaf al-indimami), where the attribute is conjoined externally (e.g., 'body is white'). The key point is that derived attribution does not require the existence of both the subject and attribute in the same external locus; it only requires the existence of the subject. Absolute attribution, covering both types, does not require the subsistence of the attribute in the external locus, only the subsistence of the described subject. However, the absolute subsistence of the attribute itself (whether mental or external) is necessary for the attribution to be meaningful. The commentator then introduces a standard objection: since attribution is a relation between two relata, the attribute must exist in the external locus. The response, from al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq and al-Dawani, is that a distinction must be made between the very attribution (nafs al-ittisaf) and the existence of the attribution (wujud al-ittisaf). Only the latter requires the external existence of both relata; the very attribution can exist without the attribute being externally present in the locus. This resolves the apparent contradiction. The commentator then refutes the view of the author of 'al-Ufuq al-Mubin' who claimed that a thing cannot be in a locus without its existence being realized there. Finally, in the 'admonition' (tabsira), the commentator clarifies that al-Sayyid's intention in speaking of 'realization of the very attribution externally' is simply the realization of the described subject such that the attribute can be derived from it. Any objection is either a denial of self-evident truth or a verbal dispute. The commentator also highlights the problem of infinite regress if one insists on the external existence of the attribution itself. Throughout, the commentator uses examples from the Islamic sciences: e.g., 'body and white' for conjunctive attribution, and 'sky and above-ness' for derived attribution.

Key Terms
الاتصاف الانضمامي
الاتصاف الانتزاعي
ظرف الاتصاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Conjunctive attribution (al-ittisaf al-indimami)
C) Absolute attribution (mutlaq al-ittisaf)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Derived attribution does not require the attribute’s external existence; it suffices that the subject exists and the attribute is derived from it.

The Objection from the Relational Nature of Attribution and its Resolution
Presents and resolves a difficulty about the existence of the attribute in attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the logical objection that attribution requires both relata to exist, and explain the distinction between the very attribution (nafs al-ittisaf) and the existence of attribution (wujud al-ittisaf) as a resolution.

Core Idea
Attribution as a relation demands existence of both relata only when considering the existence of the attribution, not the very attribution itself.

A standard objection arises: if attribution is a relation, it must need both relata to exist. This would force derived attribution to require the attribute’s existence, contradicting its nature. The solution, offered by al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq and al-Dawani, draws a subtle but crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the objection in premise form
The objector argues: Attribution is a relation (nisba). Every relation requires the existence of its two relata. Therefore, attribution requires the existence of both subject and attribute.
This seems to challenge derived attribution.
2
Identify the response's key distinction
The respondent distinguishes between 'the very attribution' (nafs al-ittisaf) and 'the existence of the attribution' (wujud al-ittisaf).
This is the core of the resolution.
3
Apply the distinction to the objection
The requirement of existence applies only to the latter (the existence of attribution), not the former. The very attribution can exist mentally or as a relation without the attribute being externally instantiated.
4
Test with examples
In conjunctive attribution, both relata exist externally, so the existence of attribution is realized. In derived attribution, only the subject exists externally; the attribution itself exists only mentally or as a relation.
This explains why derived attribution is possible.

Refuting the View of al-Ufuq al-Mubin and Clarifying al-Sayyid’s Intention
Refutes the view of author of al-Ufuq al-Mubin and clarifies the intention of al-Sayyid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flawed view of the author of al-Ufuq al-Mubin and explain why it leads to a regress, and also clarify al-Sayyid’s intended meaning regarding the realization of the very attribution externally.

Core Idea
Claiming that the very attribution must have external existence leads to either contradiction or infinite regress.

The author of ‘al-Ufuq al-Mubin’ objected that a thing cannot be in a locus without its existence being realized. The commentator refutes this by showing it either denies the obvious or leads to an impossible regress. Moreover, the commentator clarifies al-Sayyid’s intention to avoid misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
State the objection of al-Ufuq al-Mubin
He claimed that ‘the very thing being in a locus without the realization of its existence is unintelligible; for existence is the being.’
He equates ‘being in a locus’ with ‘existence in that locus.’
2
Identify the commentator’s refutation strategy
The commentator shows that this leads to an infinite regress if applied to conjunctive attribution: if the attribution itself must exist, then its existence requires another existence, and so on.
This is a reductio ad infinitum.
3
Analyze the two options presented
Either you admit a difference between the thing and its existence (thus accepting the distinction), or you deny it and face regress.
The first option is the way of al-Sayyid and al-Dawani.
4
Understand the admonition (tabsira)
The commentator clarifies that when al-Sayyid spoke of ‘realization of the very attribution externally’, he meant the realization of the described subject from which the attribute is derived, not the independent existence of the attribution.
Any objection on this basis is either a denial of self-evident truth or a verbal dispute.

بخلاف الاتصاف الانتزاعي، وهو ما كان بانتزاع الصفة؛ فإنه لا يستدعي وجودهما في ظرف الاتصاف، بل يستدعي ثبوت الموصوف فقط. فمطلق الاتصاف الشامل للانضمامي والانتزاعي لا يستدعي ثبوت الصفة في ظرفه، أي ظرف الاتصاف، بل ثبوت الموصوف. أما مطلق الثبوت، أي ثبوت الصفة سواء كان في الذهن أو في الخارج فضروري في مطلق الاتصاف؛ فإن ما لا يكون موجودًا في نفسه يستحيل أن يكون موجودًا لشيء. هذا ليس ضروريًا ولا مبرهنًا عليه، بل الضرورة شاهدة بأن الوجود في الأذهان العالية أو السافلة لغو في اتصاف الموصوف بها. نعم، يجب وجود الصفة في ظرف الاتصاف بوجود المنشأ، وإلا صارت اختراعية. ثم ههنا إشكال، وهو: أن الاتصاف نسبة وهي فرع وجود المنتسبين، فلا بد من وجود الصفة في ظرفه. أجاب عنه السيد المحقق ـ قدس سره ـ وتبعه المحقق الدواني أنه فرق بين نفس الاتصاف ووجود الاتصاف، وههنا في الخارج نفس الاتصاف، والمستدعي لوجود المنتسبين هو الثاني فقط. ووهم صاحب الأفق المبين أن كون نفس الشيء في ظرف مع عدم تحقق وجوده غير معقول؛ فإن الوجود هو الكون، ورجع عن الطريقة القويمة القديمة، وتبعه المصنف وقال: والاتصاف ليس متحققًا في الخارج، حتى يلزم تحقق الصفة فيه؛ لأنه نسبة، وكل نسبة تحققها فرع تحقق المنتسبين، بل هو متحقق في الذهن، وإن كان في الانضمامي الخارجي الموصوف متحدًا مع الصفة في الأعيان، كالجسم والأبيض، وفي الانتزاعي الخارجي منحذًا بحسب الأعيان، كالسماء والفوقية. تبصرة في تحقيق المحصورات اعلم: أن مقصود السيد ـ قدس سره الشريف ـ بتحقق نفس الاتصاف في الخارج تحقق الموصوف بحيث ينتزع منه الصفة، فإن أنكر الواهم هذا المعنى فقد خالف الضرورة، وإلا فتنازعه لفظي. ثم إنه ماذا يقول في الانضمامي الخارجي؟ فإما أن يقول أن نفسه في العين دون وجوده، فقد اعترف الفرق بين تحقق نفس الشيء وتحقق وجوده، أو يقول بتحقق وجوده فيه أيضًا، فمع كونه ضروري البطلان يفضي إلى التسلسل المحال، والله أعلم بالصواب.
Contrary to derived attribution, which is by derivation of the attribute, for it does not require their existence in the locus of attribution, but rather requires only the subsistence of the described. So absolute attribution, which includes conjunctive and derived, does not require the subsistence of the attribute in its locus, i.e., the locus of attribution, but rather the subsistence of the described. As for absolute subsistence, i.e., the subsistence of the attribute, whether in the mind or externally, it is necessary in absolute attribution; for that which does not exist in itself is impossible to exist for something. This is not necessary nor proven, rather necessity witnesses that existence in high or low minds is vain in the attribution of the described to it. Yes, the existence of the attribute in the locus of attribution is required with the existence of the source, otherwise it becomes invented. Then here is a difficulty, which is: attribution is a relation and it is a branch of the existence of the two relata, so the existence of the attribute in its locus is necessary. The chief master, may his secret be sanctified, answered it, followed by the chief al-Dawani, that he distinguished between the very attribution and the existence of the attribution, and here externally is the very attribution, and the requirer of the existence of the two relata is only the second. And the author of 'al-Ufuq al-Mubin' imagined that the very thing being in a locus without the realization of its existence is unintelligible; for existence is the 'being', and he reverted from the sound ancient method, and the author followed him and said: Attribution is not realized externally, so that the realization of the attribute in it would be necessary; because it is a relation, and every relation its realization is a branch of the realization of the two relata, rather it is realized in the mind, even if in the external conjunctive the described is united with the attribute in individuals, like body and white, and in the derived external it is separated according to individuals, like sky and above-ness. An admonition concerning the investigation of quantified propositions: Know that the intention of the master, may his noble secret be sanctified, in the realization of the very attribution externally is the realization of the described such that the attribute is derived from it; if the objector denies this meaning, he has contradicted necessity, otherwise his dispute is verbal. Then what does he say about the external conjunctive? Either he says that its very self is in the external without its existence, so he has admitted the difference between the realization of the very thing and the realization of its existence; or he says that its existence also is realized in it, then while being necessarily false it leads to impossible regress. And God knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of earlier logical positions on the nature of attribution (ittisaf). The commentator begins by distinguishing two types of attribution: derived attribution (al-ittisaf al-intiza'i), which is based on deriving an attribute from a subject (e.g., 'sky is above' where 'above' is derived from the sky's position), and conjunctive attribution (al-ittisaf al-indimami), where the attribute is conjoined externally (e.g., 'body is white'). The key point is that derived attribution does not require the existence of both the subject and attribute in the same external locus; it only requires the existence of the subject. Absolute attribution, covering both types, does not require the subsistence of the attribute in the external locus, only the subsistence of the described subject. However, the absolute subsistence of the attribute itself (whether mental or external) is necessary for the attribution to be meaningful. The commentator then introduces a standard objection: since attribution is a relation between two relata, the attribute must exist in the external locus. The response, from al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq and al-Dawani, is that a distinction must be made between the very attribution (nafs al-ittisaf) and the existence of the attribution (wujud al-ittisaf). Only the latter requires the external existence of both relata; the very attribution can exist without the attribute being externally present in the locus. This resolves the apparent contradiction. The commentator then refutes the view of the author of 'al-Ufuq al-Mubin' who claimed that a thing cannot be in a locus without its existence being realized there. Finally, in the 'admonition' (tabsira), the commentator clarifies that al-Sayyid's intention in speaking of 'realization of the very attribution externally' is simply the realization of the described subject such that the attribute can be derived from it. Any objection is either a denial of self-evident truth or a verbal dispute. The commentator also highlights the problem of infinite regress if one insists on the external existence of the attribution itself. Throughout, the commentator uses examples from the Islamic sciences: e.g., 'body and white' for conjunctive attribution, and 'sky and above-ness' for derived attribution.

Key Terms
نفس الاتصاف
وجود الاتصاف
التسلسل المحال

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of denying the distinction between the very thing and its existence in the context of conjunctive attribution?
A) It leads to a contradiction with self-evident truths.
B) It leads to an infinite regress.
C) It is a verbal dispute.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The claim that the very attribution must exist externally either collapses into a verbal dispute or leads to an infinite regress; the correct view distinguishes between the attribution and its existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Apply the infinite regress argument to the claim: 'The attribute of power (qudra) must exist as a separate entity in God's essence.' Show why this leads to regress.

Essential Attributes: Unconditional Necessity
Author responds to an objection about conditional necessity of essential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why essential attributes must be unconditionally necessary for the essence and identify the absurd consequence if they were conditional on existence.

Core Idea
Essential attributes are necessary for the essence even without existence.

In this passage, the author responds to an objection claiming that essential attributes like 'animality' for 'human' are necessary only conditionally, i.e., requiring the subject's existence. The objection might seem plausible, but the author shows it leads to an impossibility. We will unpack the reasoning to see why essential attributes are unconditionally necessary and why the alternative would imply the essence is prior to its own attribute—a clear logical absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objector's Claim
The objector suggests that essential attributes are necessary for the essence only when the essence exists. That is, they require the condition of existence (بشرط الوجود). This is a subtle point: does 'humanity' require an actual human to be true of the essence?
The term 'essential attributes' (الذاتيات) refers to properties indispensable to the thing's quiddity, like animality for human.
2
Extract the Author's Response
The author flatly rejects the condition. He says essential attributes are necessary 'always without the condition of existence' (دائما لا بشرط الوجود). They belong to the essence intrinsically, regardless of whether the essence exists in reality. This is a stronger claim: the attribute is per se necessary.
The Arabic 'لا بشرط الوجود' is a technical phrase negating the condition of existence.
3
Understand the Implication of the Alternative
If we accept the objector's view, then the existence of the essence becomes a condition for the attribute. But then the attribute would be 'made' (مجعولة) for the essence after the essence exists. That would mean the essence precedes its own essential attribute, which is impossible because an essential attribute is part of what the essence is.
The example given: 'humanity of man would be made for the essence of man'. This leads to circularity.
4
Recognise the Absurdity
The impossibility (محال) is clear: the essence cannot be prior to its own essential attribute, as that would require the essence to exist before it has its defining property. Therefore, the original objection fails—essential attributes are not conditional on existence. The author notes this conclusion does not depend on the broader debate about whether attributes are created by a new act or by the essence itself.
The author refers to prior discussion on 'essential making' (المجعولية الذاتية) but says this point is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنُوقِض بِثْبُوتِ الذَّاتِيَّاتِ للذات ؛ فَإِنَّهُ ضَرُورِيٌّ لِلذَّاتِ دَائِمَا لَا بِشَرْطِ الْوُجُودِ ، وَإِلَّا يكن ضروريا لا بشرط الوجود كان وجود الذات شرطا لَكَانَتْ حَيَوَانِيَّةُ الْإِنْسَانِ مَثَلاً مَجْعُولَةً لذات الإنسان، فيلزم تقدم الذات على الذاتي، وهو محال، فليس هذا موقوفا على بطلان المجعولية الذاتية بجعل مستأنف أو بجعل الذات، فَافْهَمْ، وقد سبق منا كلام في المجعولية الذاتية ، فتذكر وتشكر الله سبحانه ؛ فإنه ملهم الصواب.
And it was objected by the establishment of essential attributes for the essence; for it is necessary for the essence always without the condition of existence, otherwise if it were necessary only with the condition of existence, then the existence of the essence would be a condition, and then humanity of man, for example, would be made for the essence of man, leading to the priority of the essence over the essential, which is absurd. So this is not dependent on the invalidity of the essential being made by a renewed making or by the making of the essence. So understand, and there has preceded from us speech concerning essential making, so remember and thank Allah, for He is the inspirer of correctness.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding essential attributes (الذاتيات) such as 'animality' for 'human'. The objector seems to claim that essential attributes are necessary for the essence only conditionally. The response clarifies that essential attributes are necessary for the essence always (دائما) without any condition of existence. If they required the existence of the essence as a condition, then the attribute would be caused by the essence, leading to circularity (the essence would be prior to its essential attribute). The author concludes that this is not dependent on the debate about whether attributes are created by a separate act or by the essence itself. The key is that essential attributes are unconditionally necessary for the essence.

Key Terms
الذاتيات (al-dhatiyyat)
المجعولية الذاتية (al-maj‘uliyya al-dhatiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Essential attributes are necessarily and always true of the essence, without any condition of existence; the alternative leads to impossible circularity.

The Three Disjunctions and Their Two-Part Composition
Author defines three disjunctions and states their two-part composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of disjunction and state the compositional rule for each.

Core Idea
Every disjunction is a single relation between exactly two parts.

We often encounter multi-option statements like 'the concept is necessary, possible, or impossible.' This passage shows why such a statement is not a simple three-part disjunction but a compound. We'll learn the definitions of the three disjunctions and how each is composed of exactly two parts, with specific logical relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of disjunction
From the passage, note the three: real (haqiqi), maniat al-jam', maniat al-khulw. Each has a different logical property: what it prevents.
2
Define each type's logical condition
For real: prevents both conjunction and disjunction (cannot both be true nor both false). For maniat al-jam': prevents conjunction only (cannot both be true, but can both be false). For maniat al-khulw: prevents disjunction only (cannot both be false, but can both be true).
These are the standard definitions.
3
Learn the compositional rule for each
The author gives: real is composed of a proposition and its contradictory or equivalent; maniat al-jam' is composed of a proposition and what is more specific than its contradictory; maniat al-khulw is composed of a proposition and what is more general than its contradictory.
This ensures each has exactly two parts.
4
Apply to the three-part example
The example 'every concept is either necessary, possible, or impossible' is not a simple three-part disjunction. It is a compound of a categorical ('this concept is necessary') and a maniat al-khulw disjunction ('the concept is either possible or impossible'). This reduces to two parts.
Thus the apparent three parts are actually two layers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِخِلَافِ مَانِعَةِ الْجَمْع؛ إذ يجوز تركبها من ثلاثة أجزاء، لا يمكن اجتماع كل اثنين منها في الصدق، ويجوز اجتماعهما في الكذب، (وَمَانِعَة الْخُلَو)؛ إذ يجوز تركبها من ثلاثة لا يجوز اجتماع اثنين منها في الكذب، ويجوز اجتماعهما في الصدق، هذا هو المشهور . (وَذَهَبَ جَمَاعَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ الاِنْفِصَالَ مُطْلَقًا، سواء كان حقيقيا أو منع جمع أو منع خلو (لَا يَتَحَصَّلُ إِلَّا مِنْ جزئين (اثْنَيْنِ لَا أَزْيَدَ وَلَا أَنْقَصَ)، ولما كان لمتوهم أن يتوهم النقض بنحو إما أن يكون المفهوم واجبا، وإما أن يكون ممكنا، وإما أن يكون ممتنعا قال: (وَمِثْلُ كُلَّ مَنْهُوم إِمَّا وَاجِبٌ أَوْ مُمْكِنُ أَوْ مُمْتَنِعٌ مُرَكَّبٌ)، ليس من حمليات ثلاث حتى يرد نقضه، بل (مِنْ حَمْلِيَّة وَمُنْفَصِلَةٍ مانعة الخلو ؛ فإن قولنا : هذا المفهوم إما واجب» إن كذب صدق المفهوم إما ممكن أو ممتنع على سبيل منع الخلو ، وإن كذب مانعة الخلو صدقت، فينعقد منهما انفصال حقيقي، وليس مأخوذا على أنه منع جمع، حتى يرد أنهما صادقان، فكيف ينعقد انفصال حقيقي. (وَزَعَمَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنَّهُ مُطْلَقًا يُمْكِنُ تَرْكِيبُهُ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ فَوْقَ اثْنَيْنِ، وَالْحَقُّ هُوَ الثَّانِي ؛ لِأَنَّ الاِنْفِصَالَ نِسْبَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ، وَالنَّسْبَةُ الْوَاحِدَةُ لَا تُتَصَوَّرُ إِلَّا بَيْنَ اثْنَيْنِ ، وَمَا قِيلَ إِنَّ فِيهِ)، أي في هذا التعليل (مُصَادَرَةً ؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِنْ أَرَادَ) المستدل في الكبرى (أَنَّ كُلَّ نِسْبَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ انْفِصَالِيَّةٍ أَوْ غَيْرِهَا، فَهُوَ مَحَلُّ النَّزَاع) الذي هو الدعوى ، (وَإِلَّا) ، أي وإن لم يرد ذلك، بل أراد أن بعض النسب الواحدة لا تكون إلا بين اثنين، (فَلَا يَنْفَعُ) ؛ لكونه جزئيا، (فَمَدْفُوعٌ بِمَا يُدْفَعُ بِهِ ، أي المصادرة (فِي كُبْرَى) الشكل (الْأَوَّلِ)، من الفرق بين الإجمال والتفصيل، فإن المأخوذ في الكبرى محل النزاع إجمالا ، والعنوان شامل لكل نسبة إجمالا، والمأخوذ في محل النزاع النسبة الانفصالية نسبة بخصوصها، وباختلاف العنوان يختلف القضية بديهةً وكسباً، ويرتفع المصادرة. (فَتَأَمَّلْ)، فيه إشارة إلى أن الدفع لا يتم إلا إذا اعترض بلزوم المصادرة، وأما لو اقتصر على منع كلية الكبرى، بأن يقال: إنها نظرية لا بد لها من دليل فلا يتم، بل لا بد حينئذ من التمسك بدليل أو دعوى بديهة، كذا في «الحاشية» . وإذا ثبت أن الانفصال مطلقا لا يكون إلا بين اثنين: (فَالْحَقِيقِيَّةُ لَا تَتَرَكَّبُ إِلَّا مِنْ قَضِيَّةٍ وَنَقِيضِهَا أَوْ مُسَاوِيهِ)؛ فإن ارتفاع النقيضين وارتفاع قضية ومساوي نقيضها محال ، وكذا الاجتماع. (وَمَانِعَةُ الْجَمْعِ مِنْهَا وَمِمَّا هُوَ أَخَصُّ مِنْ نَقِيضِهَا)؛ فإن اجتماع الشيء مع ما هو أخص من نقيضه محال، وإلا لزم اجتماع النقيضين بخلاف الارتفاع؛ لجواز تحقق النقيض في ضمن أخص آخر. (وَمَانِعَةُ الْخُلُوِّ مِنْهَا وَمِمَّا هُوَ أَعَمُّ مِنْ نَقِيضِهَا)؛ لأن ارتفاع الشيء وأعم من نقيضه يوجب ارتفاع النقيضين، ولا استحالة في اجتماعهما؛ لجواز تحقق الأعم في ضمن أخص آخر غير النقيض . (هَذَا) ، والله أعلم بالصواب.
Unlike maniat al-jam': it may be composed of three parts, where no two can be true together but can both be false. And maniat al-khulw: it may be composed of three parts where no two can be false together but can both be true. This is the well-known view. And a group held that the disjunction absolutely, whether real, maniat al-jam', or maniat al-khulw, consists only of two parts, no more and no less. And since a deluder might delude a refutation by something like 'the concept is either necessary, or possible, or impossible', he said: 'And an example like 'every concept is either necessary or possible or impossible' is compound, not three categoricals so that a refutation would apply, but rather of a categorical and a maniat al-khulw disjunction. For when we say 'this concept is either necessary', if it is false, then 'the concept is either possible or impossible' is true on the basis of maniat al-khulw; and if the maniat al-khulw is false, it is true; so from the two a real disjunction is formed. And it is not taken as maniat al-jam' so that it would be said that they are both true; how then would a real disjunction be formed? And some claimed that absolutely it is possible to compose it from more than two parts, and the truth is the second, because the disjunction is a single relation, and a single relation can only be conceived between two. And what was said that in this reasoning there is circularity: because if the arguer intended in the major that every single relation, whether disjunctive or otherwise, that is the very point of dispute; and if not, but he intended that some single relations are only between two, then it does not profit because it is particular. So it is refuted by what refutes circularity in the first figure's major, regarding the difference between total and detail. For what is taken in the major is the point of dispute in total, and the title includes every relation in total, while what is taken in the point of dispute is the disjunctive relation specifically. And with the difference of title, the proposition differs intuitively and acquisitionally, and circularity is removed. 'So contemplate' – therein is an indication that the rebuttal is only complete if one objects on the basis of circularity. But if one merely denies the universality of the major, saying it is theoretical and needs a proof, it is not enough; rather then one must cling to a proof or claim of intuition, as in the Hashiyah. And when it is established that disjunction absolutely is only between two: then the real disjunction is composed only of a proposition and its contradictory or its equivalent, because the negation of two contradictories and the negation of a proposition and the equivalent of its contradictory are impossible, as is their conjunction. And maniat al-jam' is composed of it and what is more specific than its contradictory, because the conjunction of a thing and what is more specific than its contradictory is impossible, else the conjunction of contradictories would be required, unlike their negation because the contradictory may be realized within another more specific. And maniat al-khulw is composed of it and what is more general than its contradictory, because the negation of a thing and what is more general than its contradictory necessitates the negation of the two contradictories, and there is no impossibility in their conjunction because the more general may be realized within another more specific other than the contradictory. This, and Allah knows best the correct.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn about disjunctive propositions. It first distinguishes the two special types of disjunction: maniat al-jam' (exclusive disjunction that prevents conjunction) and maniat al-khulw (exclusive disjunction that prevents both being false). The author notes that the well-known view allows these to be composed of three parts. Then he presents a view of a group that any disjunction (whether real or the two types) can only have two parts. He anticipates an objection using the example 'every concept is either necessary, possible, or impossible', which appears to be a three-part disjunction. He explains that this is actually a compound of a categorical and a maniat al-khulw disjunction. Then he states the truth is that a disjunction is a single relation and can only be between two. He then addresses the charge of circularity (musadara) in this reasoning, explaining that the charge can be defeated by distinguishing between total and specific. He then gives the precise composition of each type: real disjunction is from a proposition and its contradictory or equivalent; maniat al-jam' is from a proposition and what is more specific than its contradictory; maniat al-khulw is from a proposition and what is more general than its contradictory. He provides the reasoning for each, based on the impossibility or possibility of conjunction and negation of contradictories.

The Argument for Two-Part Disjunction and Rebutting Circularity
Author defends the two-part disjunction view and responds to circularity charge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the argument that a disjunction must be two-part and evaluate the rebuttal of the circularity charge.

Core Idea
A single relation cannot relate more than two terms, so the two-part nature is logically necessary.

Some logicians argued that disjunctions could have more than two parts. The author defends the two-part view by first stating that a disjunction is a single relation, and a single relation can only be between two terms. But a critic charges this reasoning with circularity. We'll trace the argument and the sophisticated rebuttal using the distinction between total and specific.

Guided Path
1
State the claim and the main argument
The claim: any disjunction (real, maniat al-jam', maniat al-khulw) consists of exactly two parts. The argument: disjunction is a single relation (nisba wahida), and a single relation can only be conceived between two terms.
2
Identify the circularity objection
The objector says: In the argument, the major premise 'every single relation is only between two' either includes disjunctive relations or not. If it includes them, it is exactly the point in dispute (musadara). If it does not include them, it is a particular statement and does not prove the conclusion.
3
Analyze the rebuttal: distinction of total vs. specific
The author rebuts by saying the major premise takes 'every single relation' in a total sense (ijmal), while the dispute is about a specific kind (disjunctive relation). This distinction removes the circularity because the premise is not identical to the conclusion when considered in detail.
This is a standard move in logic to avoid circularity: differentiate the level of generality.
4
Evaluate the condition for a successful rebuttal
The author notes that the rebuttal only works if the objection is on grounds of circularity. If the objector merely denies the universality of the major premise, the rebuttal is insufficient; one would need to provide a proof or claim intuition.
The phrase 'فتأمل' hints at this nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِخِلَافِ مَانِعَةِ الْجَمْع؛ إذ يجوز تركبها من ثلاثة أجزاء، لا يمكن اجتماع كل اثنين منها في الصدق، ويجوز اجتماعهما في الكذب، (وَمَانِعَة الْخُلَو)؛ إذ يجوز تركبها من ثلاثة لا يجوز اجتماع اثنين منها في الكذب، ويجوز اجتماعهما في الصدق، هذا هو المشهور . (وَذَهَبَ جَمَاعَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ الاِنْفِصَالَ مُطْلَقًا، سواء كان حقيقيا أو منع جمع أو منع خلو (لَا يَتَحَصَّلُ إِلَّا مِنْ جزئين (اثْنَيْنِ لَا أَزْيَدَ وَلَا أَنْقَصَ)، ولما كان لمتوهم أن يتوهم النقض بنحو إما أن يكون المفهوم واجبا، وإما أن يكون ممكنا، وإما أن يكون ممتنعا قال: (وَمِثْلُ كُلَّ مَنْهُوم إِمَّا وَاجِبٌ أَوْ مُمْكِنُ أَوْ مُمْتَنِعٌ مُرَكَّبٌ)، ليس من حمليات ثلاث حتى يرد نقضه، بل (مِنْ حَمْلِيَّة وَمُنْفَصِلَةٍ مانعة الخلو ؛ فإن قولنا : هذا المفهوم إما واجب» إن كذب صدق المفهوم إما ممكن أو ممتنع على سبيل منع الخلو ، وإن كذب مانعة الخلو صدقت، فينعقد منهما انفصال حقيقي، وليس مأخوذا على أنه منع جمع، حتى يرد أنهما صادقان، فكيف ينعقد انفصال حقيقي. (وَزَعَمَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنَّهُ مُطْلَقًا يُمْكِنُ تَرْكِيبُهُ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ فَوْقَ اثْنَيْنِ، وَالْحَقُّ هُوَ الثَّانِي ؛ لِأَنَّ الاِنْفِصَالَ نِسْبَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ، وَالنَّسْبَةُ الْوَاحِدَةُ لَا تُتَصَوَّرُ إِلَّا بَيْنَ اثْنَيْنِ ، وَمَا قِيلَ إِنَّ فِيهِ)، أي في هذا التعليل (مُصَادَرَةً ؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِنْ أَرَادَ) المستدل في الكبرى (أَنَّ كُلَّ نِسْبَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ انْفِصَالِيَّةٍ أَوْ غَيْرِهَا، فَهُوَ مَحَلُّ النَّزَاع) الذي هو الدعوى ، (وَإِلَّا) ، أي وإن لم يرد ذلك، بل أراد أن بعض النسب الواحدة لا تكون إلا بين اثنين، (فَلَا يَنْفَعُ) ؛ لكونه جزئيا، (فَمَدْفُوعٌ بِمَا يُدْفَعُ بِهِ ، أي المصادرة (فِي كُبْرَى) الشكل (الْأَوَّلِ)، من الفرق بين الإجمال والتفصيل، فإن المأخوذ في الكبرى محل النزاع إجمالا ، والعنوان شامل لكل نسبة إجمالا، والمأخوذ في محل النزاع النسبة الانفصالية نسبة بخصوصها، وباختلاف العنوان يختلف القضية بديهةً وكسباً، ويرتفع المصادرة. (فَتَأَمَّلْ)، فيه إشارة إلى أن الدفع لا يتم إلا إذا اعترض بلزوم المصادرة، وأما لو اقتصر على منع كلية الكبرى، بأن يقال: إنها نظرية لا بد لها من دليل فلا يتم، بل لا بد حينئذ من التمسك بدليل أو دعوى بديهة، كذا في «الحاشية» . وإذا ثبت أن الانفصال مطلقا لا يكون إلا بين اثنين: (فَالْحَقِيقِيَّةُ لَا تَتَرَكَّبُ إِلَّا مِنْ قَضِيَّةٍ وَنَقِيضِهَا أَوْ مُسَاوِيهِ)؛ فإن ارتفاع النقيضين وارتفاع قضية ومساوي نقيضها محال ، وكذا الاجتماع. (وَمَانِعَةُ الْجَمْعِ مِنْهَا وَمِمَّا هُوَ أَخَصُّ مِنْ نَقِيضِهَا)؛ فإن اجتماع الشيء مع ما هو أخص من نقيضه محال، وإلا لزم اجتماع النقيضين بخلاف الارتفاع؛ لجواز تحقق النقيض في ضمن أخص آخر. (وَمَانِعَةُ الْخُلُوِّ مِنْهَا وَمِمَّا هُوَ أَعَمُّ مِنْ نَقِيضِهَا)؛ لأن ارتفاع الشيء وأعم من نقيضه يوجب ارتفاع النقيضين، ولا استحالة في اجتماعهما؛ لجواز تحقق الأعم في ضمن أخص آخر غير النقيض . (هَذَا) ، والله أعلم بالصواب.
Unlike maniat al-jam': it may be composed of three parts, where no two can be true together but can both be false. And maniat al-khulw: it may be composed of three parts where no two can be false together but can both be true. This is the well-known view. And a group held that the disjunction absolutely, whether real, maniat al-jam', or maniat al-khulw, consists only of two parts, no more and no less. And since a deluder might delude a refutation by something like 'the concept is either necessary, or possible, or impossible', he said: 'And an example like 'every concept is either necessary or possible or impossible' is compound, not three categoricals so that a refutation would apply, but rather of a categorical and a maniat al-khulw disjunction. For when we say 'this concept is either necessary', if it is false, then 'the concept is either possible or impossible' is true on the basis of maniat al-khulw; and if the maniat al-khulw is false, it is true; so from the two a real disjunction is formed. And it is not taken as maniat al-jam' so that it would be said that they are both true; how then would a real disjunction be formed? And some claimed that absolutely it is possible to compose it from more than two parts, and the truth is the second, because the disjunction is a single relation, and a single relation can only be conceived between two. And what was said that in this reasoning there is circularity: because if the arguer intended in the major that every single relation, whether disjunctive or otherwise, that is the very point of dispute; and if not, but he intended that some single relations are only between two, then it does not profit because it is particular. So it is refuted by what refutes circularity in the first figure's major, regarding the difference between total and detail. For what is taken in the major is the point of dispute in total, and the title includes every relation in total, while what is taken in the point of dispute is the disjunctive relation specifically. And with the difference of title, the proposition differs intuitively and acquisitionally, and circularity is removed. 'So contemplate' – therein is an indication that the rebuttal is only complete if one objects on the basis of circularity. But if one merely denies the universality of the major, saying it is theoretical and needs a proof, it is not enough; rather then one must cling to a proof or claim of intuition, as in the Hashiyah. And when it is established that disjunction absolutely is only between two: then the real disjunction is composed only of a proposition and its contradictory or its equivalent, because the negation of two contradictories and the negation of a proposition and the equivalent of its contradictory are impossible, as is their conjunction. And maniat al-jam' is composed of it and what is more specific than its contradictory, because the conjunction of a thing and what is more specific than its contradictory is impossible, else the conjunction of contradictories would be required, unlike their negation because the contradictory may be realized within another more specific. And maniat al-khulw is composed of it and what is more general than its contradictory, because the negation of a thing and what is more general than its contradictory necessitates the negation of the two contradictories, and there is no impossibility in their conjunction because the more general may be realized within another more specific other than the contradictory. This, and Allah knows best the correct.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn about disjunctive propositions. It first distinguishes the two special types of disjunction: maniat al-jam' (exclusive disjunction that prevents conjunction) and maniat al-khulw (exclusive disjunction that prevents both being false). The author notes that the well-known view allows these to be composed of three parts. Then he presents a view of a group that any disjunction (whether real or the two types) can only have two parts. He anticipates an objection using the example 'every concept is either necessary, possible, or impossible', which appears to be a three-part disjunction. He explains that this is actually a compound of a categorical and a maniat al-khulw disjunction. Then he states the truth is that a disjunction is a single relation and can only be between two. He then addresses the charge of circularity (musadara) in this reasoning, explaining that the charge can be defeated by distinguishing between total and specific. He then gives the precise composition of each type: real disjunction is from a proposition and its contradictory or equivalent; maniat al-jam' is from a proposition and what is more specific than its contradictory; maniat al-khulw is from a proposition and what is more general than its contradictory. He provides the reasoning for each, based on the impossibility or possibility of conjunction and negation of contradictories.

Understanding Dawaran and Its Limitations
Author critiques dawaran and introduces effect requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why dawaran (coextensiveness) is insufficient to prove causality and explain the requirement of effect (ta'thir) as stated by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Correlation does not imply causation – effect is essential for causality.

In this lesson, we explore the method of dawaran (also called tard wa 'aks) used by logicians to establish causality. The author of our passage critically examines this method, pointing out that mere correlation between a ruling and a proposed cause is not enough. Drawing on the authority of Imam Abu Hanifa, he emphasizes that true causality requires an effective influence (ta'thir). Understanding this critique is vital for rigorous legal reasoning in Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Define dawaran
Find the definition: dawaran is the constant accompaniment of a ruling with a cause in both existence and non-existence. It is also called tard wa 'aks.
Remember: it is based on correlation.
2
Understand the logicians' claim
The logicians claim that dawaran is a sign that the basis (madar) is a cause for the revolving (da'ir).
This is the position the author will challenge.
3
Identify the critique
The author argues that dawaran can occur in two effects of one cause, or in correlatives (mutada'ifayn). Therefore, it cannot be a reliable sign of causality.
Example: if A always accompanies B, both could be effects of C.
4
Establish the requirement of effect
The author quotes Imam Abu Hanifa: 'The cause must have an effect, either in the essence of the ruling or its type or its genus.' Dawaran alone is nothing without effect.
Effect (ta'thir) means the cause must truly influence the ruling.
5
Apply the condition to religious matters
In religious matters (shar'iyyat), causality cannot be known through dawaran alone; it must be established by text or consensus. If the premises are certain, the resulting cause is certain.
This anchors the method in revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِإِثْبَاتِ الْعِليَّةِ طُرُفٌ مذكورة في أصول الفقه، وَالْعُمْدَةُ عند أهل المنطق الدَّوَرَانُ، وَيُعَبَّرُ عَنْهُ بِالطَّرْدِ وَالْعَكْس ، وَهُوَ الاِقْتِرَانُ، أي اقتران الحكم بالعلة وُجُودًا وَعَدمَا ، قَالُوا الدَّوَرَانُ آيَةُ كَوْنِ الْمَدَارِ عِلَّةَ لِلدَّائِر. لا يخفى عليك أن مجرد الدوران قد يكون في معلولي علة واحدة، وفي المتضايفين، فكيف يكون آية للعلية، بل لا بد لها من التأثير؛ كما قال الإمام الهمام، إمام الأئمة سيد الأتقياء والعلماء، وارث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، إمامنا الأعظم إمام الكل، الإمام أبو حنيفة الكوفي، رضوان الله تعالى عليه وعلى أتباعه لا بد في العلة من التأثير، إما في عين الحكم أو نوعه أو جنسه ، وبالعكس، ولا يكفي الدوران ، بل هو ليس شيئا، ولا سبيل إلى العلم به في الشرعيات إلا إذا ثبت بنص أو إجماع، هذا أنهما إذا كانا قطعيين يفيد قطعية العلة ألبتة. فقد ظهر من وَالتَّرْدِيدُ ، وَيُسَمَّى بِالسَّبْرِ وَالتَّقْسِيمِ، وَهُوَ تَتَبَّعُ الْأَوْصَافِ، وَإِبْطَالُ بَعْضِهَا ؛ لِتَعَيُّنِ الْبَاقِي) للعلية. وهذا الطريق حجة بالاتفاق، لكن لا بد في الحصر للأوصاف من الاستعانة بالنص أو الإجماع عندنا في الشرعيات، وإن كان هذا الحصر وإبطال الباقي ظنيين أفاد الظن، وإلا أفاد القطع.
For establishing causality there are methods mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh. The mainstay according to logicians is dawaran (coextensiveness), which is expressed as tard wa 'aks (co-presence and co-absence). It is the concomitance of the ruling with the cause in existence and non-existence. They said: coextensiveness is a sign that the basis is a cause for the revolving. It is not hidden from you that mere coextensiveness may occur in two effects of one cause, and in correlatives; so how can it be a sign of causality? Rather, causality requires effect (ta'thir)—as the great Imam, the leader of the pious and learned, the inheritor of the Messenger of Allah, our greatest Imam Abu Hanifa al-Kufi—may Allah be pleased with him and his followers—said: 'The cause must have an effect, either in the essence of the ruling or its type or its genus, and vice versa. Coextensiveness is not sufficient; indeed it is nothing. There is no way to know it in religious matters unless established by text or consensus. This: when they (the premises) are certain, they yield the certainty of the cause absolutely.' Then it appears: and al-tarded (alternation), also called sabr wa taqsim (probing and division), which is the tracking of attributes and invalidating some of them so that the remaining one is determined for causality. This method is a proof by agreement, but in religious matters we must rely on text or consensus for the enumeration of attributes. If this enumeration and invalidation are probable, it yields probability; otherwise it yields certainty.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage defines the methods for establishing the 'illa (cause) in logical and legal reasoning. The author begins by noting that there are several methods mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh, but the primary one among logicians is dawaran, also called tard wa 'aks, which is the correlation of the ruling with a proposed cause in both presence and absence. However, the author immediately critiques this: mere correlation (dawaran) is not sufficient to prove causality because it can exist between two effects of a single cause or between correlatives (mutada'ifayn). For example, if two rulings always occur together, one might mistakenly think one is the cause of the other when both stem from a third cause. Therefore, causality requires actual effect (ta'thir): the cause must truly have an impact on the ruling, either directly or through its genus. The author quotes Imam Abu Hanifa to stress that dawaran alone is 'nothing' and that in religious matters (shar'iyyat) causality can only be known through text or consensus if the premises are certain. He then presents the second method: al-tarded, also known as sabr wa taqsim (probing and division). This method involves enumerating all possible attributes (awṣāf) that could be the cause and systematically eliminating those that are invalid until only one remains, which is then designated as the 'illa. This method is universally accepted as a proof (ḥujja), but the author points out a condition in religious matters: the enumeration of attributes must be supported by text or consensus. If the enumeration and elimination are probable, the resulting 'illa is only probable; if they are certain, the 'illa is certain. Thus, the text provides a nuanced view: while dawaran is criticized as insufficient, tarded (sabr wa taqsim) is accepted as valid, provided the necessary enumeration is grounded in authoritative sources.

الدَّوَرَانُ
الطَّرْدُ وَالْعَكْسُ
التَّأْثِيرُ
الْعِلَّةُ
الشَّرْعِيَّاتُ

A) Because it is not mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh
B) Because it can occur between two effects of one cause or between correlatives
C) Because it relies on text or consensus
D) Because it is always uncertain

Key Takeaway
Mere correlation (dawaran) is insufficient to prove causality; effect (ta'thir) is essential, and in religious matters, text or consensus is required.

Tarded (Sabr wa Taqsim): The Valid Method for Establishing 'Illa
Author presents tarded as the valid method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the method of tarded (sabr wa taqsim) and explain the conditions for its validity in religious matters.

Core Idea
Tarded (sabr wa taqsim) systematically eliminates all but one possible cause, yielding a valid 'illa.

Having critiqued dawaran, the author introduces a more rigorous method: al-tarded, also known as sabr wa taqsim (probing and division). This method involves listing all possible attributes that could be the cause and eliminating those that are invalid, leaving only the true 'illa. It is universally accepted as a proof, but in Islamic legal theory, the enumeration must be grounded in revelation or consensus. This lesson breaks down the procedure and its epistemological implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of tarded
Find the term: al-tarded, also called sabr wa taqsim. It is defined as tracking the attributes (tatappu' al-awsaf) and invalidating some so that the remaining one is determined as the 'illa.
Think of it as a process of elimination.
2
Understand the procedure
The jurist enumerates all possible attributes (awṣāf) that could be the cause for a ruling. Then, one by one, they are shown to be invalid (e.g., because they are not coextensive or lack effect). The remaining attribute is then the 'illa.
This is logical elimination.
3
Note the universal acceptance
The author says this method is a proof by agreement (ḥujja bil-ittifāq). It is accepted by all scholars.
Unlike dawaran, which is disputed.
4
Recognize the condition in religious matters
In religious matters (shar'iyyat), the enumeration of attributes must rely on text or consensus. This ensures that the list of possible causes is complete and valid.
Without this, the method could be arbitrary.
5
Understand the epistemological outcome
If the enumeration and elimination are probable (ẓannī), the resulting 'illa is probable. If they are certain (qaṭ'ī), the 'illa is certain.
This shows how certainty level depends on the premises.

وَلِإِثْبَاتِ الْعِليَّةِ طُرُفٌ مذكورة في أصول الفقه، وَالْعُمْدَةُ عند أهل المنطق الدَّوَرَانُ، وَيُعَبَّرُ عَنْهُ بِالطَّرْدِ وَالْعَكْس ، وَهُوَ الاِقْتِرَانُ، أي اقتران الحكم بالعلة وُجُودًا وَعَدمَا ، قَالُوا الدَّوَرَانُ آيَةُ كَوْنِ الْمَدَارِ عِلَّةَ لِلدَّائِر. لا يخفى عليك أن مجرد الدوران قد يكون في معلولي علة واحدة، وفي المتضايفين، فكيف يكون آية للعلية، بل لا بد لها من التأثير؛ كما قال الإمام الهمام، إمام الأئمة سيد الأتقياء والعلماء، وارث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، إمامنا الأعظم إمام الكل، الإمام أبو حنيفة الكوفي، رضوان الله تعالى عليه وعلى أتباعه لا بد في العلة من التأثير، إما في عين الحكم أو نوعه أو جنسه ، وبالعكس، ولا يكفي الدوران ، بل هو ليس شيئا، ولا سبيل إلى العلم به في الشرعيات إلا إذا ثبت بنص أو إجماع، هذا أنهما إذا كانا قطعيين يفيد قطعية العلة ألبتة. فقد ظهر من وَالتَّرْدِيدُ ، وَيُسَمَّى بِالسَّبْرِ وَالتَّقْسِيمِ، وَهُوَ تَتَبَّعُ الْأَوْصَافِ، وَإِبْطَالُ بَعْضِهَا ؛ لِتَعَيُّنِ الْبَاقِي) للعلية. وهذا الطريق حجة بالاتفاق، لكن لا بد في الحصر للأوصاف من الاستعانة بالنص أو الإجماع عندنا في الشرعيات، وإن كان هذا الحصر وإبطال الباقي ظنيين أفاد الظن، وإلا أفاد القطع.
For establishing causality there are methods mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh. The mainstay according to logicians is dawaran (coextensiveness), which is expressed as tard wa 'aks (co-presence and co-absence). It is the concomitance of the ruling with the cause in existence and non-existence. They said: coextensiveness is a sign that the basis is a cause for the revolving. It is not hidden from you that mere coextensiveness may occur in two effects of one cause, and in correlatives; so how can it be a sign of causality? Rather, causality requires effect (ta'thir)—as the great Imam, the leader of the pious and learned, the inheritor of the Messenger of Allah, our greatest Imam Abu Hanifa al-Kufi—may Allah be pleased with him and his followers—said: 'The cause must have an effect, either in the essence of the ruling or its type or its genus, and vice versa. Coextensiveness is not sufficient; indeed it is nothing. There is no way to know it in religious matters unless established by text or consensus. This: when they (the premises) are certain, they yield the certainty of the cause absolutely.' Then it appears: and al-tarded (alternation), also called sabr wa taqsim (probing and division), which is the tracking of attributes and invalidating some of them so that the remaining one is determined for causality. This method is a proof by agreement, but in religious matters we must rely on text or consensus for the enumeration of attributes. If this enumeration and invalidation are probable, it yields probability; otherwise it yields certainty.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage defines the methods for establishing the 'illa (cause) in logical and legal reasoning. The author begins by noting that there are several methods mentioned in Usul al-Fiqh, but the primary one among logicians is dawaran, also called tard wa 'aks, which is the correlation of the ruling with a proposed cause in both presence and absence. However, the author immediately critiques this: mere correlation (dawaran) is not sufficient to prove causality because it can exist between two effects of a single cause or between correlatives (mutada'ifayn). For example, if two rulings always occur together, one might mistakenly think one is the cause of the other when both stem from a third cause. Therefore, causality requires actual effect (ta'thir): the cause must truly have an impact on the ruling, either directly or through its genus. The author quotes Imam Abu Hanifa to stress that dawaran alone is 'nothing' and that in religious matters (shar'iyyat) causality can only be known through text or consensus if the premises are certain. He then presents the second method: al-tarded, also known as sabr wa taqsim (probing and division). This method involves enumerating all possible attributes (awṣāf) that could be the cause and systematically eliminating those that are invalid until only one remains, which is then designated as the 'illa. This method is universally accepted as a proof (ḥujja), but the author points out a condition in religious matters: the enumeration of attributes must be supported by text or consensus. If the enumeration and elimination are probable, the resulting 'illa is only probable; if they are certain, the 'illa is certain. Thus, the text provides a nuanced view: while dawaran is criticized as insufficient, tarded (sabr wa taqsim) is accepted as valid, provided the necessary enumeration is grounded in authoritative sources.

إِبْطَالُ الْبَعْضِ

الْقَطْعُ

Key Takeaway
Tarded (sabr wa taqsim) is a universally accepted method for establishing causality, but in religious matters the enumeration must be grounded in revelation or consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Fitriyyat and the Classification of Observational Propositions
Defines fitriyyat and classifies mushahedat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fitriyyat and classify observational propositions into hissiyyat, wijdaniyyat, and wahmiyyat based on the source passage.

Core Idea
Fitriyyat are propositions whose middle term is always present; observational knowledge divides by sense type.

This passage from a classical logic manual lays the groundwork for understanding the types of certain premises used in Islamic sciences. By grasping fitriyyat and the classification of mushahedat, you will be able to identify the epistemic foundation of premises in arguments from kalam, fiqh, and usul.

Guided Path
1
Define fitriyyat
Locate the definition in the Arabic: 'والفطريات، وهي ما يفتقر إلى واسطة لا تغيب عن الذهن'. Note that the middle term is always present after conceiving the extremes. This is their defining feature.
This category is also called 'propositions whose syllogisms are with them'.
2
Identify the two main branches of mushahedat
The passage divides mushahedat into hissiyyat (by external senses) and wijdaniyyat (by internal sense). External senses are the five senses; internal sense includes wijdaniyyat.
Wijdaniyyat are further divided into what is found in ourselves without instruments and wahmiyyat.
3
Locate wahmiyyat within wijdaniyyat
Wahmiyyat are a subset of wijdaniyyat that involve the estimative faculty (wahm) and are specifically about sensed things. They can be true when limited to the sensible.
Example: the judgment that a wolf has enmity is a wahmi truth about a sensed thing.
4
Recognize the limitation of sense
The passage notes that sense alone gives only particular judgments (hukm juz'i), not universal ones. Universal judgments require reason.
This is crucial for understanding why observational propositions alone cannot ground universal scientific claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْفِطَرِيَّاتُ ، وَهِيَ مَا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى وَاسِطَةٍ لَا تَغِيبُ عَنِ الذَّهْنِ) بعد تصور الطرفين، (وَتُسَمَّى قَضَايَا قِيَاسَاتُهَا مَعَهَا ، وَالْمُشَاهَدَاتُ إِمَّا بِحِسٌ ظَاهِرٍ)، من السمع والبصر والذائقة واللامسة والشامة ، (وَهِيَ الْحِرِّيَّاتُ ، أَوْ بِحِسٌ بَاطِنٍ(۲)) ، لعله أراد به قوة سوى الحس الظاهر لتدخل قوة العاقلة للنفس، (وَهِيَ الْوِجْدَانِيَّاتُ (۳) ، وَمِنْهَا) ، أي بعض الوجدانيات الْوَهْمِيَّاتُ فِي الْمَحْسُوسَاتِ). (۱) قال ابن سينا في الإشارات (٣٥٠/١): هي قضايا، إنما يصدق فيها لأجل الوسط، لكن ذلك الوسط ليس مما يعزب عن الذهن، فيحوج فيه الذهن إلى طلب، بل كلما أخطر حد المطلوب بالبال خطر الوسط بالبال ، مثل قضائنا بأن الاثنين نصف الأربعة». (۲) قال السعد في شرح العقائد النسفية (٢٦): وأما الحواس الباطنة التي تثبتها الفلاسفة فلا تتم دلائلها على الأصول الإسلامية»، قال المولى الخيالي معلقا عليه (٢٦): «فإنها مبنية على أن النفس لا تدرك الجزئيات المادية بالذات، وعلى أن الواحد لا يكون مبدأ لأثرين ، والكل باطل في الإسلام». (۳) قال صاحب المواقف (١٢٤/١): إنها قليلة النفع في العلوم ؛ لأنها غير مشتركة، فلا تقوم حجة على الغير». وقال شارح المواقف (١٢٤/١): الحسيات والبديهيات هما العمدة في العلوم ، وهما يقومان حجة على الغير. الصناعات الخمس يسمى الوهم قوة في الدماغ تدرك المعاني الجزئية التي لا يدركها الحواس، كالعداوة في الذئب، والعُطُوفة في الأب، وما يصدق بهذه الحاسة وهميات، والوهم سلطان ،القوى، له تصرف على سائر المعقولات، حتى إنه ربما يعارض العقل، ويوقعه في الغلط، فالتصديق الذي يتعلق بالمحسوسات بواسطة الوهم يكون صادقا مطابقا ، كحكمه بأن في الذئب عداوة، وبأن الكرة إذا تحركت على نفسها أحدثت من حركتها كل نقطة دائرة، فهذا حكم العقل بواسطة الوهم صادق والتصديق الذي تعلق بغير المحسوسات بوساطته يكون كاذبا ، كحكمه بأن كل موجود في مكان ، فالقسم الأول من الوجدانيات . (وَمِنْهَا (١) مَا نَجِدُهُ بِنُفُوسِنَا لَا بِآلَاتِنَا من أحوال النفس والآلات، كالحكم بأن القضية ليس فيها نسبة سوى النسبة التامة الحاكية. فلعلك تفطنت بأن المشاهدات على ثلاثة أصناف، الأول ما يدرك بالحواس الظاهرة، الثاني ما يدرك بالباطن ، ومنها الوهميات في المحسوسات الثالث ما يدرك نفوسنا، والأخيران يسميان وجدانيات(٢). ثم ليس كل تصديق يحصل بالحواس من المشاهدات، بل لا بد فيها من حكم العقل أيضا وقبولها، وإلا لكان قولنا للس راب إنه ماء يصير من المشاهدات ، وكذا سائر أغلاط الوهم والحس هذا ، والعلم الحق عند علام الغيوب العليم الخبير. (۳) وَالْحَقُّ أَنَّ الْحِسَّ لَا يُفِيدُ إِلَّا حُكْمًا جُزْئِيَّا)؛ فإن الحس لا يدرك إلا
And the innate (fitriyya) propositions: they are what need a middle term that does not leave the mind, after the two extremes are conceived. They are called propositions whose syllogisms are with them. And the observational (mushahada) [propositions] are either by external sense, like hearing, sight, taste, touch, and smell, and they are the sensory (hissiyyat), or by internal sense, and they are the intuitive (wijdaniyyat). And among them (i.e., some of the wijdaniyyat) are the estimative (wahmiyyat) in sensed things. [Footnote 1: Ibn Sina said...] [Footnote 2: al-Sa'd said...] [Footnote 3: Sahib al-Mawaqif said...] The five arts. Estimation (wahm) is called a power in the brain that perceives particular meanings not perceived by the senses, like enmity in the wolf and affection in the father. And what is believed by this sense are estimative propositions. Wahm is the sultan of the powers; it has influence over all intelligibles, so much so that it sometimes opposes reason and causes it to err. The assent that relates to sensed things through wahm is true and conforming, like its judgment that there is enmity in the wolf, and that when a sphere moves on its axis, each point of its motion traces a circle. This judgment of reason through wahm is true. And the assent that relates to non-sensed things through it is false, like its judgment that every existent is in a place. So that is the first division of the wijdaniyyat. And among them (i.e., the wijdaniyyat) is what we find in ourselves without instruments, from states of the soul and instruments, like the judgment that the proposition has no relation except the complete informative relation. Perhaps you have realized that the observational [propositions] are of three types: first, what is perceived by the external senses; second, what is perceived by the internal [sense], and among them are the wahmiyyat in sensed things; third, what is perceived by ourselves. The last two are called wijdaniyyat. Then not every assent obtained by the senses is from the observational; rather, it must also include a judgment of reason and its acceptance. Otherwise, our statement 'the mirage is water' would become observational, and similarly other errors of wahm and sense. This, and true knowledge is with the Knower of the unseen, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware. (3) The truth is that sense does not give except a particular judgment; for sense only perceives...
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory lesson. It first defines fitriyyat (innate propositions) as those requiring a middle term that never leaves the mind after the extremes are conceived; they are called 'propositions whose syllogisms are with them' (i.e., the middle term is always present). Then it divides mushahedat (observational propositions) into those by external senses (hissiyyat) and those by internal sense (wijdaniyyat). The commentator provides footnotes quoting Ibn Sina's definition of fitriyyat, al-Sa'd and al-Khayali's critique of internal senses from an Islamic perspective, and al-Mawaqif's remark that wijdaniyyat are of little use in the sciences because they are not shared. The passage then explains wahm (estimation), a power in the brain that perceives particular meanings not sensed (e.g., enmity in a wolf). Wahm can be true when applied to sensed things (e.g., judging enmity in a wolf) but false when applied to non-sensed things (e.g., judging that every existent occupies place). It then clarifies that wijdaniyyat include not only wahmiyyat but also internal experiences like the judgment that a proposition has only a complete informative relation. The passage summarizes that mushahedat are of three types: external sense perceptions, internal sense perceptions (including wahmiyyat in sensed things), and what we perceive in ourselves (without instruments). The last two are wijdaniyyat. Finally, it warns that not every sense-based assent is observational; reason must also judge, otherwise mirage would be considered water. The passage ends with a note that sense gives only particular judgments (partial, not universal). This classification is crucial for understanding the foundations of certainty in logic and the limits of sensory knowledge, especially in Islamic theology where wahm is often critiqued.

المشاهدات
الحسيَّات

According to the passage, what is the defining characteristic of fitriyyat?
A) They are known through external senses.
B) They require a middle term that is always present in the mind after the extremes are conceived.
C) They are derived from internal senses only.
D) They are particular judgments about non-sensed things.

Key Takeaway
Fitriyyat are foundational certain propositions whose middle term is always present; observational propositions are classified by source—external senses (hissiyyat) and internal senses (wijdaniyyat), with wahmiyyat as a true subset about sensed things.

?

Understanding Wahm: Its Reliability and Limits
Explains wahm and the conditions for its truthful use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify wahmiyyat and evaluate when judgments from wahm are true or false according to the passage.

Core Idea
Wahm yields truth about sensible particulars but error when applied beyond the sensible.

The passage introduces wahm (estimation) as a faculty that can be a source of true knowledge within its domain, but also a cause of error when overextended. This lesson examines how the tradition assesses wahm's reliability, which is crucial for understanding the epistemology of internal senses in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Define wahm and wahmiyyat
Locate the definition in the Arabic: 'يسمى الوهم قوة في الدماغ تدرك المعاني الجزئية التي لا يدركها الحواس'. Note that wahm perceives particular meanings (like enmity) not directly sensed.
Propositions derived from this faculty are called wahmiyyat.
2
Distinguish between true and false wahmi judgments
The passage gives examples: the judgment that a wolf has enmity (true, because it is about a sensed thing) vs. the judgment that every existent is in a place (false, because it goes beyond the sensible).
The key condition: truth is preserved only when wahm operates on the sensible.
3
Understand wahm's power and risk
Wahm is called 'sultan of the powers' and can even oppose reason, leading to error. This shows why Islamic theologians often restrict its use.
Al-Sa'd and al-Khayali (footnote 2) explicitly reject internal senses in Islamic theology.
4
Connect to the broader principle that sense gives only particular judgments
The passage concludes that sense (including wahm) gives only particular judgments; universal judgments require reason. Wahm's truth is thus limited to the particular.
This reinforces why wahmiyyat cannot serve as universal premises in scientific arguments.
